Accepting Gifts from a Slave Trader: Istihsan over Qiyas
Permissibility of accepting gifts from a slave trader with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting gifts from a slave trader and explain the role of istihsan in overriding qiyas.

Core Idea
A small trade gift from a slave is permissible by istihsan, even though qiyas forbids it.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on accepting gifts from a slave who is engaged in trade with his master's permission. The general analogy (qiyas) would prohibit it because a slave cannot make gifts, but the Hanafi school opts for istihsan based on the Prophetic practice and the necessities of commerce. You will learn the conditions that make such gifts acceptable and the evidence behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act in question? Accepting a gift from a slave trader. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz) for small items necessary for trade, and disliked (makruh tanzih) for large items like clothing or money.
The ruling varies with the value of the gift.
2
Understand the opposing qiyas
The primary analogy would forbid any gift from a slave because a slave lacks legal capacity to give gifts (tabarru'); his property belongs to his master. This is the default ruling by qiyas.
Qiyas here is based on the general principle that a slave cannot dispose of property without permission.
3
Locate the evidence for istihsan
The text cites the hadith of Salman al-Farisi, who gave a gift to the Prophet while still a slave, and the Prophet accepted it. This establishes a precedent for permitting gifts from slaves in certain contexts.
The hadith is from authentic sources and shows practical facilitation.
4
Apply the condition of 'necessity of trade'
The istihsan permits only small items that are necessary for trade, such as samples or promotional items. Large or valuable gifts (like a garment or coins) are not considered necessary and thus remain disliked.
The condition ensures that the exception does not subvert the principle that a slave cannot freely give away property.
5
Note the cross-madhhab disagreement
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may hold that any gift from a slave is invalid without the master's express permission. The Hanafi school applies istihsan to facilitate trade, relying on the Prophetic example.
This illustrates how different usul lead to different fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقبول هدية العبد إلخ: لأن ذلك من ضرورات التجارة، وقد صح أن سلمان الفارسي له أهدى إلى النبي هدية قبل أن يعتق، فقبلها النبي وكان يجيب دعوة المملوك. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٨٥/٢] وهذا هو الاستحسان والقياس أن لا يجوز؛ لأنه تبرع، والعبد ليس من أهله، لكن جوز ما ذكر لما ذكرنا تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤١٣/٨] و كره كسوته إلخ يعني كره كسوة العبد التاجر الثوب أي قبول هديته إذا كانت ثوبا، وكذا كره هديته الدراهم والدنانير؛ لأنه تبرع، والعبد ليس من أهله، ولكن جوز في الشيء اليسير للضرورة استحسانا كما مر.
And accepting the gift of a slave etc.: because that is from the necessities of trade. It is authentically reported that Salman al-Farisi (before he was freed) gave a gift to the Prophet, and the Prophet accepted it, and he used to respond to the invitation of a slave. This is istihsan (juristic preference). The analogy (qiyas) is that it is not permissible because it is a gift (tabarru') and a slave is not qualified to give gifts, but the above was permitted because of the reason mentioned. (Tatimmah al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:413) And he disliked his clothing etc.: meaning he disliked (and it is disliked) accepting a garment from a trading slave, likewise he disliked his gift of dirhams and dinars because it is a gift and a slave is not qualified, but he permitted in the case of a small thing out of necessity by istihsan, as mentioned earlier.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on accepting gifts from a slave who is engaged in trade (with his master's permission). The general principle (qiyas) would forbid it because a slave is not legally qualified to make gifts (tabarru'), as his property belongs to his master. However, by istihsan (juristic preference based on need), it is permitted for small items necessary for trade, like samples or promotional items. The proof is that Salman al-Farisi (who was a slave before being freed) gave a gift to the Prophet, and the Prophet accepted it, and he also accepted invitations from slaves. This shows that it is permissible for a slave to give away small things in the context of trade. However, the author notes that it is disliked (makruh) to accept a gift of clothing or money (dirhams and dinars) from a slave, as these are significant values. The permissibility is restricted to small, incidental items.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to need, custom, or facilitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on accepting a gift of a small item from a slave trader?
A) It is forbidden because a slave cannot own property.
B) It is permissible by istihsan for small necessary items.
C) It is absolutely permissible regardless of value.
D) It is disliked but permitted if the master agrees.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits accepting small gifts from slave traders by istihsan, balancing legal analogy with practical necessity.

The Three Categories of Transactions for Minors
Rulings on guardians buying and selling for minors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify transactions involving a minor into pure benefit, pure harm, and mixed, and state who may perform each type according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Transactions for a minor are purely beneficial, purely harmful, or mixed; only the father, grandfather, and their executors may handle mixed ones.

When dealing with a minor's property, not every transaction is allowed. The Hanafi school provides a clear framework based on benefit and harm. This lesson unpacks the three categories and the guardians authorized for each, grounded in the principle of preventing harm to the minor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The passage states that transactions concerning a minor are of three types: pure benefit (naf' mahd), pure harm (darar mahd), and mixed (mutaraddid). Understand the defining feature of each.
The categories are based on the expected outcome for the minor.
2
Examine pure benefit
Pure benefit transactions, like accepting gifts or charity, can be done by anyone in the minor's household (guardian or stranger) and even by the minor himself if discerning. No special guardianship is needed.
Hiring a wet nurse is cited as an example of pure benefit.
3
Examine pure harm
Pure harm, such as manumission or divorce, is absolutely prohibited for anyone acting on behalf of the minor. No one may perform these acts.
These actions permanently deprive the minor of rights or property.
4
Examine mixed transactions
Mixed transactions (e.g., sale or hire for profit) require careful judgment. Only the father, paternal grandfather, and their executors may conduct them, because they hold wilaya (guardianship).
The mother and other relatives lack this authority for mixed transactions.
5
Apply the framework
Given a scenario, classify the transaction and identify the authorized person. For example, selling the minor's land for profit is mixed; accepting a gift is pure benefit.
Marriage is treated separately and governed by the rules of 'asaba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشراء إلخ يعني يجوز لهؤلاء الثلاثة أن يشتروا للصغير، ويبيعوا ما لا بد منه، وذلك مثل النفقة والكسوة؛ لأنه لو لم يكن لهم ذلك لتضرر الصغير، وهو ممنوع ، وأصله : أن التصرفات على الصغير على ثلاثة أقسام: نفع محض، فيملكه كل واحد هو في عياله وليا كان أو أجنبيا كالهبة والصدقة، ويملكه الصبي بنفسه إذا كان مميزا، ونوع هو ضرر محض كالعتاق والطلاق فلا يملكه عليه ،أحد ونوع متردد بين النفع والضرر مثل البيع والإجارة للاسترباح، فلا يملكه إلا الأب والجد ووصيهما سواء كان الصغير في أيديهم أو لم يكن؛ لأنهم يتصرفون عليه بحكم الولاية، واستئجار الظئر من النوع الأول، وفيه نوع آخر، وهو الإنكاح، فيجوز لكل عصبة وذوي الأرحام عند عدم العصبات، وقد تقدم بيان ذلك في كتاب النكاح تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٢٠/٨] وتؤجر أمه إلخ: أي دون المذكورين؛ لأنها تملك إتلاف منافعه بغير عوض بأن تستخدمه، ولا يملكه هؤلاء، وهذه رواية "الجامع الصغير"، وفي رواية "القدوري": يجوز أن يؤجره الملتقط، ويسلمه في صناعة، فجعله من النوع الأول، وهذا أقرب؛ لأن فيه ضرورة ونفعا محضا للصغير. (فتح)
And buying etc.: meaning it is permissible for these three [father, grandfather, their executors] to buy for the minor and sell what is indispensable, such as food and clothing, because if they did not have that, the minor would be harmed, and harm is prohibited. The origin is that transactions concerning the minor are of three types: (1) Pure benefit - every person who is in his household, whether a guardian or a stranger, may do it, like accepting gifts and charity, and the minor himself if discerning may do it. (2) Pure harm - like manumission and divorce, no one may do it on his behalf. (3) Mixed between benefit and harm - like sale and hire for profit, only the father, paternal grandfather, and their executors may do it, whether the minor is under their care or not, because they act by virtue of guardianship. Hiring a wet nurse is of the first type. And there is another type: marriage, which is permissible for every 'asaba and dhawi al-arham in the absence of 'asaba. This has been explained in the Book of Nikah. Takmila al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 8/420] And his mother may hire him out etc.: i.e., apart from the mentioned [guardians] because she owns the disposal of his services without compensation, as she may use him, and these [guardians] do not own that. This is the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir. In the narration of al-Quduri: it is permissible for the finder (multaqit) to hire him out and hand him over to a craft. So he considered it of the first type. And this is closer because there is necessity and pure benefit for the minor. (Fath)
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage deals with the permissibility of guardians entering into transactions for minors. It first states that the father, paternal grandfather, and their executors (wasi) may buy and sell necessary items like food and clothing for the minor. The underlying principle is that transactions concerning a minor's property are categorized into three types: (1) Pure benefit (e.g., accepting gifts) - anyone in the minor's household, even a stranger, may do it, and a discerning minor may do it himself. (2) Pure harm (e.g., manumission, divorce) - no one may perform these on behalf of the minor. (3) Mixed benefit and harm (e.g., sale for profit) - only the father, grandfather, and their executors may do it because they have legal guardianship (wilaya). Hiring a wet nurse falls under pure benefit. Marriage is a separate category for agnatic relatives. Then the passage addresses hiring out the minor's services: the mother is allowed to hire out the minor (i.e., use his labor) because she owns the right to his services without compensation. The guardians mentioned earlier do not have that right. However, in a narration of al-Quduri, the finder (multaqit, a person who picks up a foundling) may hire the minor out and teach him a craft because it is pure benefit and necessity. This view is considered closer (aqrab) because it serves the minor's interest.

Key Terms
الولاية (al-wilaya): Legal guardianship over a minor's property and person, held by the father, paternal grandfather, and their executors.
الملتقط (al-multaqit): The finder of a lost child (laqit), who is responsible for his care.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who may sell the property of a minor for profit?
A) The mother
B) Any relative
C) The father, paternal grandfather, and their executors
D) The minor himself if he is discerning

Key Takeaway
Transactions for a minor are classified as pure benefit (anyone can do), pure harm (no one can do), and mixed (only father, grandfather, executor can do).

The Finder (Multaqit) and Hiring Out a Foundling
Rulings on guardians buying and selling for minors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on whether the finder of a lost child may hire out the child and compare the two narrations on this issue.

Core Idea
The finder may hire out a foundling for a craft because it is pure benefit and necessity, according to the preferred view.

A foundling (laqit) has no known guardian; the finder assumes care. But can the finder put the child to work? This lesson examines a difference in Hanafi narrations and the reasoning behind the preferred view that allows it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The passage raises the question: may the finder (multaqit) hire out the minor for a craft or apprenticeship? This arises because the finder is not a natural guardian.
The finder is like a caretaker, not a guardian with full wilaya.
2
State the narration from al-Jami' al-Saghir
In al-Jami' al-Saghir, it is mentioned that the mother may hire out the minor (use his services), but the father and other guardians do not have that right. The finder is not listed as an authorized hirer.
This implicitly restricts hiring out to only the mother.
3
State the narration from al-Quduri
Al-Quduri narrates that the finder may hire out the minor and hand him over to a craft. He classifies this as pure benefit (al-naw' al-awwal).
Al-Quduri sees it as analogous to accepting charity or hiring a wet nurse.
4
Analyze the tarjih (preference)
The commentator (Fath) says al-Quduri's view is 'aqrab (closer) because there is necessity (darura) and pure benefit (naf' mahd) for the minor.
The preference reinforces the principle that pure benefit transactions should be facilitated.
5
Apply the preferred view
In practice, a multaqit may arrange training or employment for a foundling if it is purely beneficial and necessary for the child's welfare.
This is limited to pure benefit; mixed transactions still require a proper guardian.

Source Text

وشراء إلخ يعني يجوز لهؤلاء الثلاثة أن يشتروا للصغير، ويبيعوا ما لا بد منه، وذلك مثل النفقة والكسوة؛ لأنه لو لم يكن لهم ذلك لتضرر الصغير، وهو ممنوع ، وأصله : أن التصرفات على الصغير على ثلاثة أقسام: نفع محض، فيملكه كل واحد هو في عياله وليا كان أو أجنبيا كالهبة والصدقة، ويملكه الصبي بنفسه إذا كان مميزا، ونوع هو ضرر محض كالعتاق والطلاق فلا يملكه عليه ،أحد ونوع متردد بين النفع والضرر مثل البيع والإجارة للاسترباح، فلا يملكه إلا الأب والجد ووصيهما سواء كان الصغير في أيديهم أو لم يكن؛ لأنهم يتصرفون عليه بحكم الولاية، واستئجار الظئر من النوع الأول، وفيه نوع آخر، وهو الإنكاح، فيجوز لكل عصبة وذوي الأرحام عند عدم العصبات، وقد تقدم بيان ذلك في كتاب النكاح تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٢٠/٨] وتؤجر أمه إلخ: أي دون المذكورين؛ لأنها تملك إتلاف منافعه بغير عوض بأن تستخدمه، ولا يملكه هؤلاء، وهذه رواية "الجامع الصغير"، وفي رواية "القدوري": يجوز أن يؤجره الملتقط، ويسلمه في صناعة، فجعله من النوع الأول، وهذا أقرب؛ لأن فيه ضرورة ونفعا محضا للصغير. Prohibition of Raw Grape Juice and Ruling on Tila'
Prohibition of raw grape juice and two interpretations of tila'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raw grape juice and cooked grape juice (tila'), explain the consensus proof for the prohibition of raw grape juice, and distinguish between the two interpretations of tila'.

Core Idea
Raw grape juice is haram by consensus; cooked grape juice (tila') is halal only if two-thirds evaporate.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses two key intoxicating drinks: raw grape juice (al-niy') and cooked grape juice (al-tila'). The Hanafi school is unanimous on the prohibition of raw grape juice once it ferments, based on consensus. For tila', there is an internal school difference: the relied-upon view distinguishes between tila' that has not reduced sufficiently (haram) and muthallath (halal).

Guided Path
1
Identify the drink and its condition
The text first treats al-niy' (raw juice) with three conditions: boiling (ghala), becoming strong (ishtadda), and throwing scum (qadhafa bi al-zabad). Recognize these as the signs of fermentation.
2
Locate the consensus proof
The text states 'hukmuhu bi al-ijma' (by consensus). Also the hadd punishment attaches to drinking it. Understand that this ijma proves the prohibition is definitive.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement on destroying it
The text notes disagreement on permissibility of destroying such prohibited drink. The correct view: it retains property value, so destruction only with valid purpose.
4
Examine the definition of tila'
The text gives two interpretations: (a) cooked until less than two-thirds gone (prohibited), (b) cooked until two-thirds gone (muthallath, permissible). Note that the author of al-Muhit confirms the second as correct.
5
Understand the inter-madhhab dispute
Al-Awza'i and some Mu'tazila allow the non-muthallath tila' because it is not khamr. The Hanafi response: it is like khamr because it is intoxicating and its little calls to much.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام الأشربة النيء من ماء العنب إذا غلا واشتد وقذف بالزبد، وحرم قليلها وكثيرها، رمی بالزبد وهو الرغوة والطلاء وهو العصير إن طبخ حتى ذهب أقل من ثلثيه، والسكر الثاني هو الطلاء ثلثيه أي الني من ماء العنب بفتحتين التي إلخ التي بكسر النون وتشديد الياء، قاله العيني، وتبعه في "الشرنبلالية": قال شيخنا: هو على غير المشهور كما في "المصباح"، ثم نقل عن عرمي زاده: أن النيء مهموز وزان حمل كل شيء يعالج بطبخ أو شي ولم ينضج. (فتح) إذا غلا من غلى يغلي غليا وغليانا بأن صار أسفله أعلاه وحرم إلخ: وهذا بالإجماع حتى أن وجوب الحد يتعلق بنفس الشرب؛ لأن قليله يدعو إلى كثيره ، بخلاف سائر المشروبات واختلفوا في إباحة إتلافها، فقيل: يباح، وقيل: لا إلا لغرض صحيح بأن كانت عند شريب خيف عليه الشرب، وأما إذا كانت عند صالح، فلا يباح؛ لأنه يخللها، والظاهر أن الاختلاف في إباحة إتلافها مفرع على الاختلاف في سقوط ماليتها، فمن قال: إنها مال، وهو الأصح؛ لأن الطباع تميل إليها، وتضن بها، قال: لا يباح إتلافها إلا لغرض صحيح كما سبق، ومن الناس من أنكر حرمة عينها، وزعم أن السكر حرام، وهذا باطل وكفر منه. (عيني، فتح، ملا مسكين) والطلاء إلخ: أي النوع الثاني من الأنواع الأربعة الطلاء، وهو اسم لعصير العنب إن طبخ حتى ذهب أقل من الباذق أيضا، وقيل: إذا ذهب ثلثه فهو الطلاء، وإذا ذهب نصفه فهو المنصف، وإن طبخ أدنى طبخة ويسمى فهو الباذق، والكل حرام إذا غلا واشتد وقذف بالزبد على الاختلاف السابق في القذف بالزبد، وجه الحرمة: أنه رقيق مطرب يجتمع عليه الفساق، فيحرم شربه دفعا للفساد الناشي من شربه، وقال الأوزاعي: إنه مباح؛ لأنه مشروب طيب، وليس بخمر، وبه قال بعض المعتزلة ولنا أنه كالخمر ؛ لأنه رقيق ملذ مطوب يدعو قليله إلى كثيره، والتقييد بالطبخ باعتبار الغالب؛ لأنه لا فرق بين أن يذهب ما ذهب بحر الشمس أو حر النار. واعلم أن الطلاء بهذا التفسير هو الطلاء المذكور في "الجامع الصغير"، وقد بين حكمه أنه حرام، وقال صاحب "المحيط": الطلاء اسم للمثلث وهو ما إذا طبخ من . ماء العنب حتى ذهب ،ثلثاه وبقي ثلثه وصار مسكرا، وتفسير الطلاء بهذا التفسير هو الصواب، وحكم هذا الطلاء الحل؛ لما روي أن كبار الصحابة له كانوا يشربون من ما ذهب ثلثاه، وبقي ثلثه على ما يجيء عن قريب وإنما سمي طلاء ؛ لقول عمر الله ما أشبه هذا بطلاء البعير، وهو القطران الذي يطلى به البعير إذا كان به حرب فالحاصل أن الطلاء يفسر بتفسيرين، وحكمه على أحد التفسيرين الحرمة، وعلى الآخر الحل.
The rulings of drinks: The raw (juice) from grape water when it boils and intensifies and throws scum, its little and many are prohibited. It throws scum which is foam. And al-tila' is the juice if cooked until less than two-thirds has gone, and the second sukr is al-tila' with two-thirds gone, i.e. the raw from grape water with a fat-ha, the one which is with kasra of the nun and tashdid of the ya. al-'Ayni said it, and he followed in al-Sharnablaliyya: our shaykh said: it is contrary to the well-known as in al-Misbah, then he narrated from 'Arrami Zada that al-niy' is mahmuz with the weight of 'hamal', everything that is treated with cooking or something and is not ripe. (Fath) 'When it boils' from 'ghala yaghli', that its bottom becomes its top, 'and it is prohibited' etc.: This is by consensus, such that the obligation of the hadd punishment attaches to the very drinking, because its little calls to its much, unlike other drinks. They differed on the permissibility of destroying it. It was said: it is permissible. It was said: no, except for a valid purpose, such as if it is with a drinker who fears drinking. But if it is with a righteous person, it is not permissible because he will turn it into vinegar. And apparently the disagreement on permissibility of destroying it branches from the disagreement on the removal of its value. Whoever says it is property (which is the correct view because natures incline to it and are stingy with it) says: it is not permissible to destroy it except for a valid purpose as before. Some people denied the prohibition of its essence and claimed that sukr is prohibited, and this is false and disbelief from him. ('Ayni, Fath, Mulla Miskin) 'And al-tila' etc.: i.e. the second of the four types is al-tila'. It is a name for grape juice if cooked until less than one-third is gone of the badhaq also. It was said: if one-third goes, it is al-tila'; if half goes, it is al-munsif; if cooked the slightest bit, it is called al-badhaq. All are prohibited when it boils and intensifies and throws scum, according to the previous disagreement on throwing scum. The reason for prohibition: it is thin, intoxicating, a gathering for sinners, so drinking it is prohibited to prevent the corruption arising from drinking it. al-Awza'i said: it is permissible because it is a good drink and not khamr, and some Mu'tazila said this. But we (Hanafis) say: it is like khamr because it is thin, pleasurable, and its little calls to its much. The qualification with cooking is based on the prevailing case, because there is no difference between the removal happening by sun heat or fire heat. Know that al-tila' with this interpretation is the tila' mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir, and its ruling is explained as prohibited. The author of al-Muhit said: al-tila' is a name for al-muthallath, which is when grape water is cooked until two-thirds go and one-third remains and it becomes intoxicating. The interpretation of al-tila' with this interpretation is correct. The ruling of this tila' is permissible, because it is narrated that senior Companions used to drink that which had two-thirds gone and one-third remained, as will come shortly. It is only called tila' because of the saying of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) 'How similar this is to the tar of the camel', which is the tar with which the camel is smeared if it has mange. The conclusion is that al-tila' is interpreted with two interpretations, and its ruling according to one interpretation is prohibition, and according to the other is permissibility.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding intoxicating drinks. It begins with the ruling on raw grape juice (al-niy'): if it boils, becomes strong, and throws scum (froths), then even a small amount is prohibited by consensus. The reason given is that a small amount invites drinking a large amount, unlike other drinks. There is disagreement on whether it is permissible to destroy such drink: the correct view (as stated) is that it is property and cannot be destroyed except for a valid purpose (e.g., if a drinker fears he will consume it). The text emphatically states that denying its essential prohibition is disbelief. It then moves to the second type, al-tila' (cooked grape juice). There is disagreement on the definition of tila'. According to one interpretation (from al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-'Ayni), tila' is juice cooked until less than two-thirds have evaporated, and its ruling is prohibition. According to another interpretation (from Sahib al-Muhit), tila' is al-muthallath: juice cooked until two-thirds have evaporated and one-third remains. The correct view according to the commentator is the latter, and its ruling is permissible (halal), based on the practice of senior Companions including Umar (RA). The commentator then notes that there are two interpretations of tila' with opposite rulings. The passage also includes a brief inter-madhhab dispute: al-Awza'i and some Mu'tazila consider such drinks permissible because they are not khamr, but the Hanafi position is that they are similar to khamr because they are thin intoxicants that lead to corruption.

Key Terms
النيء (al-niy'): Raw grape juice that has not been cooked.
الغليان (al-ghalyan): Boiling or fermentation of liquids.
الاشتداد (al-ishtidad): Becoming strong/intoxicating.
القذف بالزبد (al-qadhf bi al-zabad): Throwing scum or foam, indicating full fermentation.
الطلاء (al-tila'): Cooked grape juice. Two definitions: (1) cooked until less than two-thirds gone; (2) cooked until two-thirds gone (muthallath).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct interpretation in the text, what is the ruling on 'tila'' defined as grape juice cooked until two-thirds have evaporated?
A) It is haram
B) It is halal
C) It is makruh
D) It is mubah but disliked

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits raw grape juice by consensus, and for cooked grape juice, the relied-upon view permits the muthallath (two-thirds evaporated) while prohibiting lesser cooking.

Prohibition of Date Wine (Sukr) and Raisin Infusion (Naqi' al-Zabib): Conditions and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Prohibition of sukr and naqi' al-zabib and condition of frothing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sukr and naqi' al-zabib, identify the condition of frothing as disputed within the school, and apply the ruling to a scenario.

Core Idea
Sukr and naqi' al-zabib are haram when intoxicating; Abu Hanifa requires frothing, the Sahibayn require only boiling.

In this passage, al-Marghinani clarifies the prohibition of three drinks: tila', sukr, and naqi' al-zabib. He distinguishes them from khamr and highlights a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the condition of frothing (al-qadhf bi al-zabad). Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for correctly applying the ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the drinks and their basis
Recognize that sukr is from fresh dates, naqi' from raisins, and tila' from grapes (already discussed). Note their raw (ni') form.
These are distinct from khamr which is from grapes and intoxicating in any quantity.
2
Determine the prohibition conditions
According to the text, these drinks are prohibited when they 'boil and intensify' (ghala wa ishtadda). What does this imply?
Boiling indicates fermentation; intensifying indicates alcohol content.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Compare Abu Hanifa's requirement of frothing (qadhf bi al-zabad) with the Sahibayn's view that boiling suffices.
This difference stems from analogies: Abu Hanifa analogizes to raw grape juice; Sahibayn analogize to khamr.
4
Evaluate the evidence (dalil)
Note the hadith 'Khamr comes from these two trees' and the consensus of the Sahaba, which the Hanafis use. Opponents cite Quran 16:67.
The Quranic verse is interpreted as referring to the period before prohibition.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Given a drink that boils but does not froth: what is the ruling according to each imam?
Practice: Abu Hanifa says halal; Sahibayn say haram.

والسكر إلخ: أي النوع الثالث من الأشربة المحرمة السكر، وهو بفتحتين مشتق من سكرت الريح إذا سكنت، وإنما يحرم إذا قذف بالزبد، وقبله حلال، وقال شريك بن عبد الله: هو مباح وإن قذف بالزبد؛ لقوله تعالى: تَتَّخِذُونَ مِنْهُ سَكَرا وَرِزْقًا حَسَنام (النحل: (٦٧) امتن علينا به، والامتنان لا يتحقق بالمحرم، ولنا قوله : "الخمر من هاتين الشجرتين" الحديث، ولإجماع الصحابة والآية محمولة على الابتداء حين كانت الأشربة مباحة؛ =  كتاب الأشربة ٣٦٠ أحكام الأشربة أي الثلاثة الأخيرة " وهو النيء من ماء الرطب، ونقيع الزبيب: وهو النيء من ماء الزبيب، والكل حرام إذا صار مسكرا أي الرابع نقيع الزبيب إذا غلا واشتد، ،، وحرمتها دون حرمة الخمر، فلا يكفر مستحلها بخلاف الخمر، الأشربة الثلاثة ولكن يضلل هذه الثلاثة لأن الآية مكية، وحرمت الخمر بالمدينة، وهذا على تقدير أن يكون المراد بالآية الامتنان، وقيل: أريد بها التوبيخ، معناها - والله أعلم - أنتم لسفاهتكم تتخذون منه سكرا وتدعونه رزقا حسنا. فتح الله المعين، تبيين الحقائق) وهو النيء إلخ : اعلم أن الأشربة التي تتخذ من التمر ثلاثة: أحدها السكر، وثانيها النبيذ، وهو ما طبخ أدنى طبخة، وهو حلال كما يأتي، وثالثها الفضيخ، وهو التيء من ماء البسر المذنب مشتق من الفضخ بالضاد والخاء المعجمتين، وهو الكسر، سمي به؛ لأنه يكسر ويجعل في جب، ويصب عليه الماء الحار لتخرج حلاوته، وحكم الفضيخ كالسكر، : فلو قال المصنف مكان السكر التيء من ماء التمر لشمل السكر والفضيخ فإن التمر اسم جنس يشمل البسر والرطب. ماء الزبيب لما روي عن ابن عباس للهما "أنه عليه كان ينقع له الزبيب فيشربه اليوم، وبعد الغد إلى مساء الثالثة، ثم يأمر به فيسقى الخدم ، رواه مسلم، فإن بقي شيء أهرقه أو أمر به فأهريق. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٩٥/٢] والكل حرام إلخ أي الثلاثة الأخيرة، وإنما فسر قوله: "والكل" "حرام بذلك، ولم يجعله شاملا للخمر؛ لئلا يكون قوله: "إذا غلا "واشتد" لغوا بالنسبة للخمر. (فتح) إذا غلا واشتد إلخ أي يحرم كل واحد من الطلاء والسكر ونقيع الزبيب إذا غلا واشتد، فالغليان والاشتداد شرط لحرمة الثلاثة الأخيرة. واعلم أن القذف بالزبد بعد الغليان شرط الحرمة هذه الثلاثة عند أبي حنيفة كما كان شرطا في التيء من ماء العنب، وعندهما لا يشترط القذف، بل يكفي الغليان كما كان في الخمر، وإذا عرفت هذا، فاعلم أن ظاهر قوله: "إذا غلا واشتد يدل على أن القذف بالزبد ليس بشرط في حرمة هذه المسألة كما هو مذهبهما، وعلى هذا إما أن يقال: إنه اختار مذهبهما كبقية المتون أو يقال: إنه لم يختر مذهبهما بل اختار مذهب الإمام، ولكنه ترك قيد القذف اعتمادا على ما سبق في الخمر والحاصل أنه إذا غلا واشتد وقذف بالزبد حرم اتفاقا، وإن لم يغل و لم يشتد لا يحرم اتفاقا وإن غلا واشتد و لم يقذف فعندهما يحرم، وعنده: لا. دون حرمة الخمر إلخ لأن حرمة الخمر قطعية وحرمة هذه الثلاثة بالاجتهاد، حتى قال الأوزاعي بإباحة الأول والثالث منها، وشريك بإباحة الثاني ولقائل أن يقول: إن السكر استدللنا على حرمته بإجماع الصحابة، وقد تقرر أن الإجماع دليل قطعي فيكفر مستحلها، فكيف قلتم لا يكفر مستحلها؟ ويجاب بأنه قد يكون نقل الإجماع بطريق الآحاد ، فلا يفيد القطع، والمنقول في حرمة السكر من هذا القبيل. (عيني، تكملة) بخلاف الخمر إلخ: فإن مستحل الخمر يكون كافرا لما ذكرنا، ولا يجوز بيعها، ولا يضمن متلفها إلا أن تكون لذمي، ويحد شاربها ولو ،قطرة ولا يحد بشرب هذه الثلاثة ما لم يسكر منها ونجاستها خفيفة في رواية، وغليظة في رواية، ومحصل ما يستفاد من الدر": أن الفتوى على تغليظ النجاسة في الطلاء كالخمر، وأما غيره فقد اختلف الترجيح فيه وجاز ، وضمن متلفها عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : لا يجوز بيعها، ولا يضمن متلفها،
'And al-sukr etc.': i.e., the third type of prohibited drinks is al-sukr. It is with two fathas, derived from 'sakarat al-rih' when it calms. It is only prohibited when it throws scum; before that it is halal. Shuraik ibn 'Abd Allah said: it is permissible even if it throws scum, because of His statement: 'You take from it intoxicants and good provision' (Surah al-Nahl, 67). He conferred favor upon us through it, and favor cannot be realized with something prohibited. Our proof is the hadith 'Khamr comes from these two trees' and the consensus of the Companions. The verse is interpreted as referring to the beginning when drinks were permissible. = [PAGE_361] Book of Drinks 360 Rulings of drinks Meaning the last three 'And it is the raw from fresh dates juice, and infusion of raisins: it is the raw from raisin juice. All are prohibited when it becomes intoxicating.' i.e., the fourth, infusion of raisins when it boils and intensifies. Their prohibition is lower than the prohibition of khamr, so one who considers them permissible is not a disbeliever, unlike khamr. The three drinks [do not make one a disbeliever] but they lead to misguidance. Because the verse is Meccan, and khamr was prohibited in Medina. This is on the assumption that the verse means favor; it is also said that it meant reprimand: its meaning (and Allah knows best) is 'You, due to your foolishness, take intoxicants from it and leave good provision.' (Fath Allah al-Mu'in, Tabyin al-Haqa'iq) 'And it is the raw etc.': Know that the drinks taken from dates are three: one is al-sukr, second is al-nabidh (cooked slightly, which is halal as will come), third is al-fadikh, which is the raw from unripe dates called 'al-mudhnib', derived from 'al-fadkh' meaning breaking; named so because it is broken and placed in a jar, and hot water poured on it to extract its sweetness. The ruling of al-fadikh is like al-sukr. If the author had said 'raw from date water' instead of 'sukr', it would have included sukr and fadikh, because 'tamr' is a generic term covering both unripe and ripe dates. Raisin water: because it is narrated from Ibn 'Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) that 'he (peace be upon him) had raisins steeped for him, and he would drink it that day and the next day until the evening of the third day, then he would order it to be given to the servants to drink, narrated by Muslim. If anything remained, he would pour it out or order it to be poured out.' (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/395) 'And all are prohibited etc.': meaning the last three. He only interpreted 'all' as prohibited in that way, and did not make it include khamr, so that his statement 'if it boils and intensifies' would not be superfluous for khamr. (Fath) 'If it boils and intensifies etc.': i.e., each of tila', sukr, and infusion of raisins is prohibited when it boils and intensifies. So boiling and intensifying are a condition for the prohibition of the last three. Know that throwing scum after boiling is a condition for the prohibition of these three according to Abu Hanifa, just as it was a condition for the raw from grape water. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), throwing scum is not necessary; rather, boiling is sufficient as it was for khamr. Now that you know this, know that the apparent meaning of his statement 'if it boils and intensifies' indicates that throwing scum is not a condition for prohibition in this issue, as is their (the two's) madhhab. Based on this, it may be said that he chose their madhhab like other texts, or it may be said that he did not choose their madhhab but chose the Imam's madhhab, but omitted the condition of throwing scum relying on what preceded regarding khamr. The conclusion: if it boils, intensifies, and throws scum, it is prohibited by agreement. If it does not boil and intensify, it is not prohibited by agreement. If it boils and intensifies but does not throw scum, then according to the two it is prohibited, and according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is not. 'Less than the prohibition of khamr etc.' because the prohibition of khamr is definitive, and the prohibition of these three is by ijtihad. Even al-Awza'i permitted the first and third, and Shuraik permitted the second. One might say: we deduced the prohibition of sukr by the consensus of the Companions, and consensus is a definitive proof, so one who permits it becomes a disbeliever. Why then do you say that one who permits it does not become a disbeliever? The answer: the transmission of consensus may be through ahad (solitary) chains, not giving certainty, and the transmitted prohibition of sukr is of this type. ('Ayni, Takmila) 'Unlike khamr etc.': for the one who considers khamr permissible becomes a disbeliever as we mentioned. It cannot be sold, and one who destroys it does not guarantee it unless it belongs to a dhimmi. The drinker of it is whipped even if a drop, and the drinker of these three is not whipped unless he becomes intoxicated by them. Their impurity is light in one narration and severe in another. The summary of what is understood from al-Durr: the fatwa is on the severity of impurity in tila' like khamr. As for other than tila', the tarjih differs. It is permissible (to sell?) And the one who destroys it guarantees it according to Abu Hanifa. The two say: it is not permissible to sell it, and the one who destroys it does not guarantee it.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of prohibited drinks, focusing on the third type, al-sukr (date wine), and the fourth, naqi' al-zabib (raisin infusion). Sukr is defined as the raw juice of fresh dates; it is prohibited only when it froths (qadhf bi al-zabad). Some, like Shuraik, argued it is permissible even if frothing, citing the Quranic verse (al-Nahl 67). But the Hanafi position relies on the hadith 'Khamr comes from these two trees' (dates and grapes) and the consensus of the Sahaba. The verse is interpreted as referring to the time before prohibition. The passage also introduces al-fadikh, a drink from unripe dates, with the same ruling as sukr. Regarding raisin infusion, it is allowed if drunk within three days lest it ferment; if it remains longer, it must be discarded. The key ruling is that all these three drinks (tila', sukr, naqi' al-zabib) are prohibited when they boil and intensify. However, there is a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: for Abu Hanifa, frothing (qadhf bi al-zabad) is an additional condition for prohibition; for Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two), boiling and intensifying suffice. The text notes that the matn's wording 'if it boils and intensifies' seems to follow the view of the two, but it may be simply relying on the earlier condition for khamr. The consequence is that if a drink boils and intensifies but does not froth, it is not prohibited according to Abu Hanifa, but it is according to the two. The prohibition of these three is less severe than khamr: one who considers them permissible is not a disbeliever (but is misguided), unlike the one who declares khamr permissible. The hadd punishment applies to these only if intoxication occurs, whereas for khamr, the mere act of drinking (even a drop) triggers the hadd. There is also a dispute on the impurity (najasa) of these drinks: some say it is light, others severe; the relied-upon fatwa is that tila' is like khamr in impurity. Finally, there is a difference on guarantee: Abu Hanifa says the destroyer guarantees, while the two say no.

Key Terms
السكر (al-sukr): Raw date wine; a type of intoxicating drink from dates.
نقيع الزبيب (naqi' al-zabib): Raisin infusion; raw juice from raisins.
الفضيخ (al-fadikh): Drink made from unripe dates by soaking in hot water.
القذف بالزبد (al-qadhf bi al-zabad): Throwing scum/foam indicating full fermentation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition does Abu Hanifa require for the prohibition of sukr, over and above the condition of boiling?
A) The drink must be made from grapes
B) The drink must be cooked until two-thirds evaporates
C) The drink must throw scum (froth)
D) The drink must be stored in a clay pot

Key Takeaway
Sukr and naqi' al-zabib become prohibited when intoxicating, but the condition of frothing is disputed within the Hanafi school; the less severe prohibition means the drinker is not a disbeliever.

6 min
Nabidh of Dates and Raisins: Ruling and Conditions
Defines and proves permissibility of nabidh from dates/raisins with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nabidh of dates and raisins, identify the conditions for its permissibility, and explain the intra-Hanafi and cross-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Nabidh of dates or raisins is halal only if slightly cooked and drunk without amusement; otherwise haram by consensus.

In this passage, we examine the first type of permissible beverages: nabidh (fruit infusion) made from dates alone or raisins alone. The Hanafi school, particularly Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, consider it permissible under specific conditions, while Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i hold it to be forbidden. Understanding the conditions and the basis of the disagreement is essential for correctly applying the ruling today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Nabidh is a drink made by soaking dates or raisins in water. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, it is mubah (permissible) if cooked the slightest amount (adna tabkha) and drunk without amusement (lahw) or pleasure (tarab). Without these conditions, it is haram by consensus.
The permissibility applies to each fruit alone; mixing dates and raisins is prohibited by hadith.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is a hadith from Abu Qatada in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim: 'Do not make nabidh from unripe dates and ripe dates together, nor from ripe dates and raisins together, but make nabidh from each one separately.'
The hadith explicitly permits each alone.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition of mixing implies permission for each alone. The command 'but make nabidh from each one separately' (ولكن انتبذوا كل واحد منهما على حدة) indicates that each alone is permissible.
This is a zanni (speculative) dalil, but sufficient for establishing permissibility in the absence of a clear prohibition.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that nabidh from dates or raisins is haram, even if cooked, because it can become intoxicating. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf maintain permissibility based on the hadith and the practice of the Companions (e.g., the Badriyun).
The disagreement is both intra-Hanafi (Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad) and cross-madhhab (Hanafi vs. Shafi'i).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Although Abu Hanifa strongly argued for permissibility, the later fatwa (relied-upon position) is on the view of Imam Muhammad: nabidh is haram due to the potential for intoxication.
This shift reflects the principle of sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking means to harm).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نبيذ التمر والزبيب إلخ: أي حل نبيذ التمر ونبيذ الزبيب إن طبخ أدنى طبخة، وإن اشتد وقذف بالزبد إذا شربه بلا لهو وطرب؛ لما روي عن أبي قتادة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: "لا تنتبذوا الزهو والرطب جميعا، ولا تنتبذوا الرطب والزبيب جميعا، ولكن انتبذوا كل واحد منهما على حدة"، رواه مسلم والبخاري وهذا نص على أن كل واحد منهما على الانفراد يحل، وعند محمد والشافعي حرام ولو شرب باللهو والطرب فهو حرام بالاتفاق. أدلّة حله أيضا ما قال في "الاختيار": وعن ابن أبي ليلى قال: أشهد على البدريين من أصحاب رسول الله ومن أنهم يشربون النبيذ في الجرار الخضر، وقد نقل ذلك عن أكثر الصحابة ومشاهيرهم قولا وفعلا، حتى قال أبو حنيفة: إنه مما يجب اعتقاد حله؛ لئلا يؤدي إلى تفسيق الصحابة، وفي "المعراج": قال أبو حنيفة: لو أعطيت الدنيا بحذافيرها لا أفتي بحرمتها؛ لأن فيه تفسيق بعض الصحابة، ولو أعطيت الدنيا لشربها لا أشربها؛ لأنه لا ضرورة فيه، وهذا غاية تقواه (عيني، فتح وغيرهما)
Nabidh of dates and raisins etc.: That is, the permissibility of nabidh of dates and nabidh of raisins if cooked the slightest cooking, even if it becomes strong and throws foam, when he drinks it without amusement and [musical] pleasure. For what was narrated from Abu Qatada that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not make nabidh from unripe dates and ripe dates together, nor from ripe dates and raisins together, but make nabidh from each one separately.' Muslim and Bukhari narrated it. This is a text that each one alone is permissible. And according to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i it is forbidden. And if drunk with amusement and pleasure, it is forbidden by consensus. Among the proofs of its permissibility is also what was said in al-Ikhtiyar: from Ibn Abi Layla, he said: I bear witness over the Badriyun among the Companions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that they drink nabidh in green jars. And that has been transmitted from most of the Companions and their prominent figures, in word and deed. Until Abu Hanifa said: It is among that which it is obligatory to believe its permissibility, lest it lead to declaring the Companions deviant. And in al-Mi'raj: Abu Hanifa said: If I were given the whole world, I would not give a fatwa of its prohibition, because therein is declaring some Companions deviant. And if I were given the world to drink it, I would not drink it, because there is no necessity in it. And this is the utmost of his piety. (Ayni, Fath, and others)
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof addressing the first type of permissible beverages: nabidh (a drink made by soaking fruit in water) from dates alone or raisins alone. The ruling is that it is halal when cooked the slightest amount, even if it becomes strong and frothy, provided it is not drunk with amusement or musical pleasure. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade mixing dates and raisins but allowed each separately. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that it is permissible; Muhammad and al-Shafi'i say it is haram. If drunk with amusement, it is haram by consensus. Additional proof is the practice of the Companions (Badriyun) who drank such nabidh. Abu Hanifa emphasized that to declare it haram would be tantamount to declaring those Companions deviant, which is not permissible. However, he personally avoided it due to piety. The fatwa is on the view of Muhammad (that it is haram), as will be mentioned later.

Key Terms
نبيذ (nabidh): A drink made by soaking dates, raisins, or other fruits in water until the water extracts flavor; may be cooked or uncooked.
أدنى طبخة (adna tabkha): The slightest cooking, meaning just heating the mixture slightly so that it begins to change.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Being drunk with amusement and pleasure
C) Being made in a green jar
D) Being mixed with honey

Key Takeaway
Nabidh of dates or raisins is halal only when slightly cooked and drunk without amusement, but the relied-upon fatwa (Muhammad) considers it haram due to potential intoxication.

Second permissible drink: Mixture of dates and raisins together
Defines and proves permissibility of mixing dates and raisins together in nabidh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mixing dates and raisins in nabidh and identify the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
The mixture of dates and raisins in nabidh is permissible when cooked, based on the Prophet's practice.

This lesson examines the second type of permissible beverages in the Hanafi school: the mixture of dates and raisins. While the basic rule about nabidh is permissibility, the mixture requires specific conditions. We will explore the evidence from the Sunnah and the scholarly difference within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The mixture of date-water and raisin-water (al-khalitan). What is the hukm according to the author? It is halal (permissible), but only when cooked slightly.
The ruling is mubah according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; haram according to Muhammad.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Aisha (radiyallahu anha) in Sunan Ibn Majah: she made nabidh for the Prophet by mixing dates and raisins in a waterskin.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly shows that the Prophet drank nabidh made from a mixture of dates and raisins. This indicates permissibility.
The proof is direct action (fi'l) of the Prophet.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Muhammad al-Shaybani considers it haram. Also, the Shafi'i school holds it haram due to prohibitions against mixing dates and raisins.
The text reconciles by interpreting prohibitions as referring to raw mixing.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities (as indicated in the text) give fatwa on Muhammad's view, making the operative ruling haram.
Thus, while the stronger proof supports permissibility, the precautionary fatwa is prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخليطان أي الثاني من الأشربة الأربعة الخليطان، وهو أن يجمع بين ماء التمر وماء الزبيب، فيطبخ أدنى طبخة، ويترك إلى أن يغلي ويشتد وإنما كان حلالا؛ لما روي عن عائشة لما أنها قالت كنا ننتبذ لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في سقاء، فنأخذ قبضة من تمر وقبضة من زبيب فنطرحهما فيه، ثم نصب عليه الماء، فننتبذه غدوة، فيشربه عشية، وننتبذه عشية فيشربه غدوة، رواه ابن ماجه. وروي عن ابن زياد قال: سقاني ابن عمر شربة ما كدت أهتدي إلى أهلي، فغدوت إليه الغد، فأخبرته بذلك، من قال: ما زدناك على عجوة وزبيب"، وهو محمول على المطبوخ؛ لأن المروي عن ابن عمر حرمة نقيع الزبيب النيء منه، وما ورد من النهي محمول على الابتداء، أو على غير المطبوخ جمعا بين الأدلة، وبالأخير يحصل التوفيق، ويندفع التعارض عما نقل عن ابن عمر لهلهلهله مما يقتضي المعارضة بين قوله وفعله. (عيني، فتح، مسكين)
And the two mixtures: that is, the second of the four beverages: the two mixtures. It is that one combines date-water and raisin-water, cooks it the slightest cooking, leaves it until it boils and becomes strong. And it was permissible because of what was narrated from Aisha, that she said: We used to make nabidh for the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in a waterskin. We would take a handful of dates and a handful of raisins and throw them into it, then pour water on it. We would make nabidh in the morning and he would drink it in the evening, and we would make nabidh in the evening and he would drink it in the morning. Ibn Majah narrated it. And it was narrated from Ibn Ziyad, he said: Ibn Umar gave me a drink that hardly could I find my way to my family. So I went to him the next morning and informed him of that. He said: We did not add anything beyond excellent dates and raisins. And it is interpreted as cooked; because what is narrated from Ibn Umar is the prohibition of raw raisin infusion. And what came of prohibition is interpreted as referring to the initial [permissibility], or to the uncooked, to reconcile the proofs. And by the latter, harmony is achieved and the contradiction is repelled from what was narrated from Ibn Umar [؟] which would imply contradiction between his statement and action. (Ayni, Fath, Miskin)
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the second type of permissible beverages: the mixture of dates and raisins together in nabidh. The ruling is that it is halal when cooked slightly and left to ferment. The proof is the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as described by Aisha, where she would mix dates and raisins together for his nabidh. There is an apparent contradiction with Ibn Umar's action and statement, but the Hanafi scholars resolve it by interpreting that the prohibition applies only to raw (uncooked) infusion, and that Ibn Umar's drink was cooked. Thus, the mixture is permissible if cooked.

Key Terms
الخليطان (al-khalitan): The mixture of date-water and raisin-water together in nabidh.

Key Takeaway

Nabidh from Non-Date/Grape Sources: Halal Unconditionally
Declares all nabidh from non-date/grape sources halal unconditionally

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nabidh from honey, figs, wheat, barley, and corn, explain the proof from the hadith restricting khamr, and identify the intra-Hanafi and cross-madhhab disagreements.

Core Idea
Only drinks from dates and grapes are khamr; all other nabidh is halal unless it intoxicates.

This lesson focuses on the third type of permissible beverages in Hanafi fiqh: nabidh made from honey, figs, grains, and other non-date/grape sources. Unlike the stricter rules for date and grape wine, the Hanafi school holds these drinks to be halal unconditionally—whether cooked or uncooked—based on a prophetic hadith that explicitly restricts the term 'khamr' (and thus its prohibition) to the date-palm and grapevine. However, this ruling is not without internal and external debate, which we will examine.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage declares that nabidh from honey, figs, wheat, barley, and corn is halal unconditionally. Note that this includes both cooked and uncooked forms. The key factor is that a small amount does not lead to intoxication.
The ruling applies to any source other than dates and grapes.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is the hadith: 'Khamr is from these two trees: the date-palm and the grapevine.' This hadith is narrated by Muslim, Ahmad, and others. It is a hadith ahad with zanni thubut.
The hadith restricts the definition of khamr to two specific sources.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly limits the term 'khamr' to dates and grapes. Therefore, any intoxicating drink from other sources is not called khamr and does not carry the same ruling of intrinsic impurity (najis) or prohibition in any amount. The Hanafi school distinguishes between khamr (impure and haram in any quantity) and other intoxicants (haram only when consumed to intoxication).
This is a linguistic and legal restriction (takhsis) based on the hadith.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani reportedly held that all intoxicating nabidh—including from honey, figs, grains—is haram, similar to khamr. The mufta bihi (operative position) among later Hanafis often follows Muhammad's view, making these drinks haram if they are intoxicating, even in small amounts.
This difference is based on whether the hadith is understood restrictively or as a general rule.
5
Evaluate the cross-madhhab disagreement
The Shafi'i school and others hold that any intoxicating drink is khamr and thus haram and impure, regardless of source. Their proof is the general prohibition of intoxicants and analogical reasoning. The Hanafi response is that the hadith provides a specific restriction that overrides general analogies.
This disagreement affects the outcome for drinks like beer or nabidh from grains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونبيذ العسل والتين إلخ : أي النوع الثالث نبيذ العسل والتين والبر والشعير والذرة فهو حلال، سواء طبخ أو لم يطبخ؛ لأن قليله لا يفضي إلى الكثير كيفما كان؛ لقوله عليه: "الخمر من هاتين الشجرتين: النخلة والعنبة"، رواه مسلم وأحمد ،وآخرون فخص التحريم بهما، والمراد بيان الحكم أي حكمهما واحد؛ لأن كل واحد منهما يسمى خمرا حقيقة. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٩٦/٢]
And nabidh of honey and figs etc.: That is, the third type: nabidh of honey, figs, wheat, barley, and corn. So it is halal, whether cooked or not, because a small amount of it does not lead to a large amount in any case, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Wine (khamr) comes from these two trees: the date-palm and the grapevine.' Muslim, Ahmad, and others narrated it. So He restricted prohibition to them two. And the intent is to clarify the ruling, i.e., their ruling is the same; because each one of them is called khamr in reality. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/396]
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the third type of permissible beverages: nabidh from honey, figs, wheat, barley, and corn. Unlike the first two types, these are halal unconditionally, whether cooked or uncooked, because a small amount does not lead to intoxication. The proof is the prophetic hadith that wine (khamr) is specifically from dates and grapes (the two trees). Therefore, any intoxicant from other sources is not khamr and is permissible unless it intoxicates in large quantities. The Hanafi school holds that only khamr (grape wine) is intrinsically impure and haram; other intoxicants are haram only if consumed to intoxication.

Key Terms
خمر (khamr): Wine specifically from grapes (or dates), which is intrinsically impure and haram in any amount.
نبيذ (nabidh): A beverage made by soaking fruits, grains, or honey in water; may become intoxicating if left to ferment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because khamr is only from dates and grapes
D) Because they are fruits of paradise

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, nabidh from non-date/grape sources is halal unconditionally because the hadith restricts the term 'khamr' to dates and grapes, though later fatwa often follows Imam Muhammad's stricter view.

The Fourth Permissible Drink: Muthallath and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
States permissibility of muthallath and presents intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on muthallath, identify the mufta bihi, and explain the legal consequences for hadd and divorce.

Core Idea
Muthallath is halal for Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf but haram according to the relied-upon view of Muhammad.

This passage addresses the ruling of grape juice boiled down to one third (muthallath). It presents a major intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit it based on Companion practice, while Muhammad deems it haram due to the general prohibition of intoxicants. Understanding this difference and why the fatwa follows Muhammad's view is crucial for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two positions
State the act (consuming muthallath) and the two positions: Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf say halal, Muhammad says haram.
The act is specifically grape juice cooked until two-thirds evaporates.
2
Examine the proof for Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
They rely on narrated practices of Companions (Umar, Abu Musa, etc.) and the assertion that muthallath does not intoxicate.
They consider the drink non-intoxicating based on empirical observation.
3
Examine Muhammad's proof
Muhammad cites general hadiths: 'Every intoxicant is khamr and every intoxicant is haram' and 'What intoxicates in large amounts, a small amount is haram.'
These hadiths establish a universal principle.
4
Understand the tarjih (preference)
The text explicitly states 'wa al-fatwa 'ala qawl Muhammad' – the fatwa follows Muhammad's view.
Later Hanafi masters adopted Muhammad's stricter view for caution.
5
Note the thamarah (practical consequences)
According to the two, no hadd penalty for intoxication and divorce not valid; according to Muhammad, hadd applies and divorce counts.
The mufta bihi follows Muhammad, so these consequences apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمثلث العنبي إلخ: أي النوع الرابع: المثلث العنبي، وهو ما طبخ من ماء العنب حتى يذهب ثلثاه، ويبقى الثلث، وهو حلال وإن غلى واشتد؛ لما روي عن أبي موسى الأشعري رضي الله عنه "أنه كان يشرب من الطلاء ما ذهب ثلثاه وبقي الثلث" رواه النسائي، وله مثله عن أبي الدرداء، وقال البخاري: رأى عمر وأبو عبيدة ومعاذ من شرب الطلاء على الثلث وشرب البراء، وأبو جحيفة على النصف، وقال أبو داود سألت أحمد عن شرب الطلاء إذا ذهب ثلثاه، وبقي ثلثه فقال: لا بأس به، قلت: إنهم يقولون : إنه يسكر، فقال: لا يسكر، ولو كان يسكر لما أحله . انه عمر وهذا كله قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وقال محمد والثلاثة الأشربة الأربعة المذكورة حرام جميعها مطلقا قليلها وكثيرها؛ لقوله عليه: "كل" مسكر خمر وكل مسكر حرام ، رواه مسلم من رواية ابن عمر، وعن ابن عمر أنه عليه قال: "ما أسكر كثيره فقليله حرام"، رواه أحمد وابن ماجه والدار قطني وصححه، والفتوى على قول محمد. وهذا الاختلاف فيما إذا قصد به التقوى دون التلهي وإن قصد به التلهي فهو حرام بالإجماع، ولهذا كان ينبغي للمصنف أن يذكر التقييد بقوله: "بلا لهو وطرب" بعد الرابع، ليكون قيدا للكل، وإذا كان مباحا عندهما، فلا يحد شاربه، وإن سكر منه، ولا يقع طلاق السكران منه بمنزلة النائم وذاهب العقل بالبنج ولبن الرماك، وعن محمد يحد إذا سكر منه، ويقع طلاقه إذا طلق امرأته وهو سكران منه كما في الأشربة المحرمة. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٩٦/٢، ٣٩٧] (رد المحتار وغيرهما)
And the 'muthallath 'inabi' etc.: That is, the fourth type: the grape muthallath. It is what is cooked from grape juice until two-thirds go away and one-third remains. It is halal even if it boils and becomes strong. Because of what was narrated from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari (may Allah be pleased with him) that he used to drink from tila' (thick grape syrup) from which two-thirds had gone and one-third remained. Narrated by al-Nasa'i. And similar from Abu al-Darda'. Al-Bukhari said: Umar, Abu Ubayda, and Mu'adh saw drinking tila' at one-third, and al-Bara' and Abu Juhaifa drank at half. Abu Dawud said: I asked Ahmad about drinking tila' when two-thirds go and one-third remains; he said: no problem. I said: they say it intoxicates. He said: it does not intoxicate; if it intoxicates, he would not permit it. That is Umar's [practice]. All this is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad and the three [imams?] said: The four mentioned beverages are all absolutely haram, their small and large amounts, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Every intoxicant is khamr and every intoxicant is haram' narrated by Muslim on the authority of Ibn Umar, and from Ibn Umar that he (peace be upon him) said: 'What intoxicates in large amounts, a small amount is haram.' Ahmad, Ibn Majah, and al-Daraqutni narrated it and authenticated it. And the fatwa is on the view of Muhammad. This difference applies when the intention is piety without diversion; but if intended for diversion, it is haram by consensus. Hence the author should have mentioned the restriction 'without amusement and pleasure' after the fourth, to be a condition for all. And when it is permissible according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), then its drinker is not to be punished with the hadd penalty even if he becomes intoxicated from it, and his divorce while intoxicated from it does not take effect, similar to a sleeping person or one whose mind is gone due to banj (narcotic) or mare's milk. And from Muhammad: he is to be punished with hadd if he becomes intoxicated from it, and his divorce if he divorces his wife while intoxicated from it, as in the case of prohibited beverages.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the fourth type of permissible beverages: grape juice cooked until two-thirds evaporates (muthallath). According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, this is halal even if it becomes strong and potentially intoxicating, based on the practice of many Companions including Umar and Abu Musa. Muhammad considers all four types haram absolutely, based on general hadiths about intoxicants. The fatwa is on Muhammad's view. The difference only applies when the drink is consumed without frivolity; with frivolity it is haram unanimously. The text also discusses legal consequences: for Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, one who drinks this and becomes intoxicated is not subject to hadd penalty, and his divorce does not count. Muhammad holds that such a person is subject to hadd and his divorce counts.

Key Terms
المثلث العنبي (al-muthallath al-'inabi): Grape juice boiled until two-thirds evaporates, leaving one-third; also called tila' or muthallath.
طلاء (tila'): Thick grape syrup, often referring to muthallath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (fatwa), what is the ruling of muthallath (grape juice reduced to one third)?
A) Halal absolutely
B) Haram
C) Makruh
D) Halal only if not intoxicating

Key Takeaway
Muthallath is considered haram in the mufta bihi position due to the general prohibition of intoxicants, despite a valid difference from earlier Hanafi authorities.

Permissibility of making nabidh in various vessels
Abrogates earlier prohibition of making nabidh in specific vessels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on making nabidh in any vessel and apply the condition that the drink must not be intoxicating.

Core Idea
The earlier prohibition on specific vessels is abrogated; any vessel is permissible as long as the drink is not intoxicating.

You may have heard that certain vessels like gourds or pitch-lined jars are prohibited for making nabidh. This lesson clarifies that this prohibition was abrogated by a later hadith, which now permits any vessel—with one crucial condition: the drink itself must not be intoxicating. Let's examine the evidence and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the earlier prohibition
Recall that the Prophet initially forbade making nabidh in four specific vessels: dubba' (gourd), hantam (green/red clay jars), muzaffat (pitch-lined vessels), and naqir (hollowed logs). This was due to accelerated fermentation.
These vessels were common in early Medina.
2
Understand the later hadith as abrogating
The later hadith (from Sahih Muslim) states: 'I had forbidden you from drinks in leather containers, but now drink from every vessel, provided you do not drink an intoxicant.' This explicitly lifts the vessel restriction.
The Arabic word 'zurūf al-adam' refers to leather containers, but the general permission covers all vessels.
3
Derive the general permissibility
The command 'drink from every vessel' (fashrabū fī kulli wiā') is a general permission, making nabidh in any vessel mubah (permissible).
This is a clear example of naskh (abrogation) of a previous ruling.
4
Apply the condition
The only remaining restriction is that the drink itself must not be intoxicating (muskir). If the nabidh becomes intoxicating, it becomes haram regardless of the vessel.
The condition is substantive, not procedural: it focuses on the drink's effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the permissibility of making nabidh etc.: That is, the permissibility of making nabidh in duba' (gourd), and hantam (with fat-ha on the ha, sukun on the nun, fat-ha on the ta) - they are red jars, and it is said green jars that used to be brought to Medina containing wine. And muzaffat is the vessel whose interior is coated with zift (pitch), and naqir is the root of a wood hollowed out. Due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'I had forbidden you from drinks in leather containers, but now drink from every vessel, provided you do not drink an intoxicant.' Narrated by Muslim and others. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/397]
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the permissibility of making nabidh in specific types of vessels. Earlier, the Prophet had forbidden making nabidh in green jars (hantam), gourds (duba'), pitch-lined vessels (muzaffat), and hollowed logs (naqir) because they accelerated fermentation. Later, this prohibition was abrogated, and it became permissible to make nabidh in any vessel as long as the drink itself is not intoxicating. The proof is the later hadith where the Prophet lifted the vessel restriction and only prohibited the intoxicant itself.

Key Terms
الدباء (al-dubba'): Gourd, a type of vessel made from a dried gourd or pumpkin.
الحنتم (al-hantam): Green or red clay jars, originally used to transport wine to Medina.
المزفت (al-muzaffat): Vessel coated inside with pitch (zift).
النقير (al-naqir): Hollowed out log or stump used as a container.
الانتباذ (al-intibadh): The process of making nabidh (a non-intoxicating date infusion).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

intermediate
10 min
The Definition and Ruling of Rahn (Pledge)
Defines rahn and explains the ruling with correction about binding nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of rahn, identify its pillars and conditions, and explain the correct Hanafi position regarding its binding nature with reference to Quran and Qiyas.

Core Idea
Rahn is concluded by offer and acceptance but becomes binding only after possession (qabd).

This lesson introduces the contract of rahn (pledge or mortgage), a key security mechanism in Islamic finance. The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq provides the definition, the legal evidence, and a critical correction: the common printed wording 'binding by offer and acceptance' is erroneous. Instead, rahn is merely concluded by offer/acceptance and requires possession (qabd) to become binding. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rules of pledge contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its definition
Read the definition of rahn: 'It is the detention of a thing due to a right that can be collected from it, like a debt.' Note the key elements: detention, a right, and the possibility of collection.
The definition excludes penalties like hudud and qisas where the right is not monetary.
2
Locate the primary evidence (Quran and Sunnah)
Find the Quranic verse cited: 'So a pledge [handed over]' (al-Baqarah 2:283). Also note the sunnah of the Prophet pawning his armor. Understand that the word 'maqbuda' (taken into possession) indicates the importance of possession.
The verse is the cornerstone; the sunnah provides practical application.
3
Analyze the qiyas (analogy) to suretyship
The text argues that rahn is permissible by analogy to kafala (suretyship). Just as a surety secures the obligation side of a debt, rahn secures the collection side, and is even more appropriate since collection is the primary goal.
This qiyas is used to justify the permissibility of rahn alongside the revealed evidence.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi correction
The printed edition states 'la'zima bi ijab wa qabul' (binding by offer/acceptance). The commentary corrects this: it should be 'yan'aqid bi ijab wa qabul' (concluded by offer/acceptance) and completion by qabd. Understand that rahn is a gratuitous contract, similar to gifts, and thus not binding until possession.
This correction is emphasized by al-Ayni and al-Takmila and is the mufta bihi position.
5
State the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon Hanafi position: Rahn is concluded (in'iqad) by ijab and qabul, but it becomes binding (luzum) only after the pledgee takes possession (qabd). Without possession, either party can withdraw.
This ruling applies to all gratuitous contracts: they are not binding until delivery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرهن
تعريف الرهن وحكمه
هو حبس شيء بحق يمكن استيفاؤه منه كالدين ولزم بإيجاب وقبول، أي الرهن في الشرع
من الشيء المرهون
كتاب الرهن وجه مناسبة كتاب" الرهن لكتاب الصيد من حيث أن كل واحد من الرهن والصيد سبب لتحصيل المال تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٦٨/٨] وقال في "ملا" مسكين: المناسبة بين الكتابين أن الصيد لا يملك إلا بالأخذ، وكذلك الرهن لا يملك إلا بالقبض، ثم شرعية الرهن تثبت بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع، أما الكتاب فقوله تعالى: ﴿فَرِهَانٌ مَقْبُوضَةٌ (البقرة: (٢٨٣)، والسنة ما روي أنه عليه رهن درعه عند أبي شحم اليهودي بالمدينة، وبعث عليه والناس يتعاملونه، فأقرهم عليه وعليه الإجماع؛ ولأنه وثيقة في جانب الاستيفاء، فيجوز كما تجوز الوثيقة في جانب الوجوب، وهي الكفالة بيانه: أن للدين طرفين طرف الوجوب، وطرف الاستيفاء؛ لأنه يجب أولا في الذمة ثم يستوفى المال بعد ذلك، ثم الوثيقة لطرف الوجوب الذي يختص بالذمة، وهي الكفالة جائزة، فكذا الوثيقة التي تختص بالمال بل بطريق الأولى؛ لأن الاستيفاء هو المقصود، والوجوب وسيلة إليه تكملة ملا مسكين فتح هو حبس إلخ: اعلم أن الرهن في اللغة مطلق الحبس، قال الله تعالى: ﴿ كُلُّ نَفْسٍ بِمَا كَسَبَتْ رَهِينَةٌ (المدثر:٣٨) ويطلق الرهن على المرهون تسمية للمفعول باسم المصدر ، يقال : رهنت الرجل شيئا، ورهنت عنده وأرهنته لغة فيه، والجمع رهان ورهون ورهن، وفي الشرع ما بينه بقوله: "هو حبس" إلخ أي الرهن حبس شيء بسبب حق يمكن استيفاء ذلك الحق من ذلك الشيء الذي هو رهن، واحترز بقوله: "يمكن استيفاءه منه عن الحدود والقصاص. (عيني) كالدين: توضيح لقوله: "بحق يمكن استيفاؤه منه ؛ لأن الدين هو الحق الممكن استيفاؤه من الرهن؛ لعدم تعيينه، فعلى هذا لا يجوز الرهن إلا بالدين؛ لأن العين لا يمكن استيفاؤه من الرهن، فلا يجوز بها إلا إذا كانت مضمونة بنفسها كالمغصوب والمهر وبدل الخلع وبدل الصلح عن دم العمد ؛ لأن الموجب الأصلي فيها المثل أو القيمة، ورد العين مخلص على ما عليه الجمهور، وهو دين، ولهذا تصح الكفالة به، والإبراء عن قيمته، ويمنع وجوب الزكاة على من هو في يده ماله بقدر القيمة، ولو كان الواجب هو العين لما ثبتت هذه الأحكام بخلاف الأعيان غير المضمونة كالأمانات، أو المضمونة بغيرها كالمبيع في يد البائع حيث لا يجوز الرهن لعدم وجوبها. (عيني باختصار) ولزم بإيجاب إلخ : هكذا هو في النسخ المطبوعة، وكذا أخذه صاحب "التكملة" و"ملا مسكين"، ولذا قال في "التكملة" [٤٧٠/٨] : وهذا سهو، فإن الرهن لا يلزم بالإيجاب والقبول؛ لأنه تبرع، ولكنه ينعقد بهما، ويتم بالقبض، فيلزم، ووقع في "الطائي" و "العيني" مكان قوله: "لزم" "وينعقد بإيجاب وقبول"، وهذا هو الصحيح، قال العيني. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٠٤/٢] في شرح هذا القول: لأنه عقد فأشبه سائر العقود، ووقع في بعض النسخ: ولزم بإيجاب وقبول واعتمد الشارح الزيلعي عليه ثم قال: وهذا سهو إلخ، ولو اعتمد على النسخة الصحيحة لما
نسبه إلى السهو.
Book of Rahn. Definition of Rahn and its ruling. It is the detention of a thing due to a right that can be collected from it, like a debt, and it becomes binding by offer and acceptance. Meaning of rahn in law: from the thing pledged. Book of Rahn: the suitability of placing the Book of Rahn after the Book of Hunting, since both rahn and hunting are means of acquiring wealth. Completion from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 8/468. And he said in 'Mulla Miskin': the connection between the two books is that hunting is only owned by taking, and likewise rahn is only owned by taking possession. Then the legality of rahn is established by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus. As for the Book, His statement: 'So a pledge [handed over]' (al-Baqarah 2:283). As for the Sunnah, it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) pawned his armor with Abu Shiham al-Yahudi in Medina, and he (peace be upon him) sent [letters] and the people did business with it, so he ratified them. And there is consensus on it; and because it is a security on the side of collection, it is permissible just as a security on the side of obligation is permissible, and that is suretyship. Explanation: The debt has two sides: the side of obligation and the side of collection; because it is first owed in the dhimmah then the property is collected afterwards. Then security for the side of obligation which is specific to the dhimmah, which is suretyship, is permissible, so too the security that is specific to the property, rather even more appropriate, because collection is the objective and obligation is a means to it. Completion from Mulla Miskin. 'He is habs' etc.: Know that rahn in language is absolute detention. Allah says: 'Every soul for what it has earned is detained' (al-Muddaththir 38). And rahn is used for the thing pledged, naming the object with the name of the gerund. It is said: I pledged something to a man, and I pledged with him, and I caused him to pledge is a language variant. The plural is rihan, ruhun, and rahn. And in law, it is what he clarified by saying: 'It is the detention' etc., meaning rahn is the detention of a thing due to a right that can be collected from that thing which is a pledge. And he distinguished by his saying: 'can be collected from it' from hudud and qisas. (Ayni). 'Like a debt': clarification of his saying: 'due to a right that can be collected from it'; because debt is the right from which collection from the pledge is possible due to its non-specification. Thus, rahn is only permissible for a debt; because a specific item cannot be collected from the pledge, so it is not permissible for it except if it is itself guaranteed, like the stolen property, dower, compensation for khul', and blood-money for intentional homicide; because the original obligatory [item] in them is the equivalent or value, and the return of the specific item is a release according to the majority, and it is a debt. For this reason suretyship for it is valid, and acquittal from its value, and it prevents the obligation of zakah on the one in whose hand his property is of equivalent value. If the obligatory were the specific item, these rulings would not be established, unlike non-guaranteed specific items like trusts, or those guaranteed by others like the sold item in the seller's hand, where rahn is not permissible due to lack of obligation. (Ayni with abbreviation). 'And it becomes binding by offer and acceptance' etc.: This is what is in the printed versions, and so the author of al-Takmila and Mulla Miskin took it, so he said in al-Takmila [8/470]: This is a slip, because rahn is not binding by offer and acceptance; because it is a donation, but it is concluded by them, and it is completed by possession, so it becomes binding. And in al-Ta'i and al-Ayni, instead of his saying 'la'zima' they wrote 'yan'aqid bi ijab wa qabul', and this is the correct. Al-Ayni said in Rami al-Haqa'iq [2/404] in explanation of this statement: because it is a contract, so it resembles other contracts. And in some copies it occurred: 'la'zima bi ijab wa qabul', and the commentator al-Zayla'i relied upon it, then he said: This is a slip, etc. If he had relied on the correct copy, he would not have attributed it to a slip.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Rahn (Pledge) begins with the definition and ruling of the rahn contract. The author defines rahn as the detention of a property as security for a right, typically a debt, that can be satisfied from that property. He then states that rahn becomes binding 'by offer and acceptance', but immediately the commentary clarifies that this is a textual error in some editions. The correct Hanafi position, as explained by al-Ayni and others, is that rahn is concluded (yan'aqid) by offer and acceptance but completed (yatimmu) by possession (qabd), and only then does it become binding (yalmazu). This is because rahn is a gratuitous contract (tabarru'), similar to gifts, which are not binding until delivery. The passage then provides the legal basis for rahn: the Quranic verse 'fa rihanun maqbuda' (a pledge with possession, al-Baqarah 2:283) and the Sunnah practice of the Prophet pawning his armor with a Jewish man. Ijma (consensus) is also cited. An interesting discussion is the suitability of placing the Rahn chapter after the Hunting chapter—both involve acquiring benefit through taking possession. The passage also delves into linguistic aspects of the word 'rahn' and elaborates that rahn is only valid for a debt or a guaranteed obligation, not for unguaranteed specific items. The key takeaway for the student is that the Hanafi school distinguishes between the conclusion of the contract (in'iqad) and its binding effect (luzum), with possession being the critical factor.

Key Terms
الرهن (ar-rahn): The contract of pledge/mortgage where property is detained as security for a debt.
الحبس (al-habs): Detention or confinement of property as a security.
إيجاب وقبول (ijab wa qabul): Offer and acceptance – the two pillars of contract conclusion.
القبض (al-qabd): Possession – actual or constructive taking of the pledged property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the correct ruling regarding the binding nature of a rahn contract?
A) It is binding immediately upon offer and acceptance.
B) It is concluded by offer and acceptance but becomes binding only after possession.
C) It is binding only if a written contract is made.
D) It is not binding at all.

Key Takeaway
Rahn is a contract concluded by offer and acceptance, but it only becomes binding upon delivery of possession to the pledgee.
