Territorial Jurisdiction of a Judge
A ruling on territorial jurisdiction of a judge over property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a judge's jurisdiction over property outside his district and identify the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
A judge's jurisdiction is generally territorial, but for movable property the correct opinion extends it.

This ruling addresses a question of judicial authority: can a judge adjudicate over property that lies outside his territorial jurisdiction (wilayah)? The passage presents the original rule from Kanz al-Daqa'iq that such a judgment is invalid, but then notes that later authorities, including al-Tanwir, consider the correct view that it is valid, especially for movables.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling
The original text states: 'A property not within the judge's jurisdiction, his judgment therein is not valid.'
This is the statement from Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
2
Recognize the ikhtilaf among scholars
Some scholars consider the location, others consider the parties (ahl).
3
Note the relied-upon opinion (mufta bihi)
Al-Tanwir and others hold that the judgment is valid for movables, and this is the fatwa.
The judge should write to the local judge for execution.
4
Apply the distinction between movables and immovables
For immovables, the original rule may still apply; but for movables, jurisdiction is not an issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الخنثى
مسائل شتی
ما دمت، ببخاری، فخرج منها ورجع وفعل لا يحنث باع أتانا لا يدخل جحشها في البيع. والعقار المتنازع فيه لا يخرج من يد ذي اليد ما لم يبرهن المدعي. عقار لا في ولاية القاضي لا يصح قضاؤه فيه. إذا قضى القاضي في حادثة ببينة، ثم قال: رجعت عن قضائي، أو بدا لي غير ذلك، أو وقعت في تلبيس الشهود، أو أبطلت حكمي، قال قال من قال وهو ظاهر، أقول: وهذه المسألة وكذا التي بعدها أعني: قوله باع أتانا إلخ مذكورتان في النسخ المطبوعة. الكنز الموجودة عندي لكن لم يأخذهما أحد من الشراح مثل الطائي وملا مسكين وصاحب "التكملة"، وأما العيني فلم تذكر فيه هاتان المسألتان على ما نقله في حاشية الكنز المطبوع في "بمب"، وذكرهما في حاشية الكنز المطبوع بمطبع الأحمدي، و لم أظفر على أصل نسخة العيني لأنظر ما فيه فليتنبه له وعلى كل حال فالمراد ظاهر.
أتانا باع إلخ: أي إن باع رجل أتانا لا يدخل ولدها المنفصل في البيع وهو ظاهر أيضا، وقد ذكرت ما يتعلق بهذه المسألة في الصفحة الماضية عند قوله: إن فعلت كذا، فليذكر ما لم يبرهن المدعي أي إذا ادعى عقارا لا يكتفي بذكر المدعي أنه في يد المدعى عليه حتى تصح دعواه، بل لابد أن يبرهن أنه في يده، أو يعلم القاضي بذلك في الصحيح؛ لأن يد المدعى عليه لابد منه لتصح الدعوى عليه، وهو شرط فيها ويحتمل أن يكون في يد غيره، فبإقامة البينة تنفي تهمة المواضعة فيقضي القاضي عليه بإخراجه من يده لتحقق يده بخلاف المنقول؛ لأن اليد فيه مشاهدة، فلا يحتاج إلى إثباتها بالبينة، فإن قيل: هذه مكررة من قوله في كتاب الدعوى: "ولا تثبت اليد في العقار بتصادقهما بل ببينة أو إعلام، قاض بخلاف المنقول؟ قلنا لا تكرار؛ لأن تلك بالنظر إلى ثبوت اليد، وهذه بالنظر إلى أن القاضي هل يملك إخراجها من ذي اليد؟ تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤١٩/٩] يصح قضاؤه إلخ: أي إذا كان عقار متنازع فيه وليس في ولاية القاضي لا يصح قضاؤه في ذلك العقار؛ لأنه لا ولاية له في ذلك المكان، وقد اختلف المشايخ هل يعتبر المكان أو الأهل؟ فقيل: يعتبر المكان، وقيل: الأهل، حتى لا ينفذ قضاؤه في غير ذلك المكان على قول من اعتبر المكان، ولا في غير ذلك الأهل على قول من اعتبر الأهل، لا وإن خرج القاضي مع الخليفة من المصر، قضى وإن خرج وحده لم يجز قضاؤه. رمز الحقائق: ٥٠٦/٢] قال في الفتح واعلم أن ما جزم به في "الكنز" و"الملتقى" خلاف الصحيح، قال في "التنوير" وشرحه: عقار لا في ولاية القاضي، يصح قضاؤه فيه كمنقول هو الصحيح، وتقدم في القضاء أن المصر ليس بشرط فيه، به يفتى، ويكتب بالحكم القاضي تلك الناحية ليأمره بالتسليم. ببينة إلخ: تقييده بالبينة يشير إلى الاحتراز عما لو قضى بعلمه أو بخلاف مذهبه أو ظهر خطؤه، ففي هذه الثلاث يجوز له الرجوع، وفي "التنوير" وشرحه قال الشهود قضيت وأنكر القاضي، فالقول له، به يفتى، خلافا لمحمد ما لم ينفذه قاض آخر، فحينئذ يكون القول قوله؛ لوجود قضاء الثاني. (فتح)
ونحو ذلك، لا يعتبر، والقضاء ماض إن كان بعد دعوى صحيحة وشهادة مستقيمة. خبأ قوما، ثم سأل رجلا عن شيء، فأقر به، وهم يرونه ويسمعون كلامه، وهو لا يراهم جازت شهادتهم، وإن سمعوا كلامه ولم يروه لا باع عقارا وبعض أقاربه حاضر يعلم البيع ثم ادعى، لا يسمع دعواه. ونحو ذلك: نحو أن يقول: رجعت عن حكمي أو فسخته ونحوها لا يعتبر أي قول القاضي في هذه الصور؛ لتعلق حق الغير به، وهو المدعي. (فتح) والقضاء ماض إلخ لأن رأيه الأول قد ترجح بالقضاء، فلا ينقض باجتهاد مثله، ولا يملك الرجوع عنه، ولا إبطاله؛ لأنه تعلق به حق الغير، وهو المدعي، ألا ترى أن الشهادة لما اتصلت بالقضاء لا يصح رجوعه، ولا يملك إبطالها لما ذكرنا فكذا القضاء تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٢٠/٩] بعد دعوى صحيحة إلخ وهي ما يتعلق بها أحكامها من إحضار الخصم والمطالبة بالجواب والإتيان بالبينة. (ملا مسكين) شهادة مستقيمة وهي شهادة عدول إذا أجمعت شرائط الصحة احتراز عما إذا قال ذلك بعد دعوى فاسدة أو شهادة غير مستقيمة، وصورة الدعوى الفاسدة إذا ادعى محدودا و لم يبين أنه كرم أو أرض، والشهود شهدوا كذلك ملا) (مسكين رجلا آخر عن شيء مثل دينا له. جازت شهادتهم إلخ: أي شهادة القوم الذين خبأهم على ذلك الرجل بالإقرار؛ لأن الإقرار موجب بنفسه، وقد علموه، وهو أي العلم يكفي في أداء الشهادة، قال الله تعالى: ﴿إِلَّا مَنْ شَهِدَ بِالْحَقِّ وَهُمْ يَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ (الزخرف:٨٦) وقال عليه: "إذا علمت مثل الشمس فاشهد وإلا فدع تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤۲۰/۹] لا : يعني وإن سمع القوم الذين خبأهم كلام ذلك الرجل المسئول و لم يروه، لا تجوز شهادتهم عليه؛ لأن النغمة تشبه النغمة، فيحتمل أن يكون المقر، غيره فلا يجوز لهم أن يشهدوا عليه مع الاحتمال، إلا إذا كانوا دخلوا البيت وعلموا أنه ليس فيه أحد سواهم، ثم جلسوا على الباب وليس للبيت مسلك غيره، ثم دخل رجل، فسمعوا إقرار الداخل، و لم يروه وقت الإقرار؛ لأن العلم حصل لهم في هذه الصورة، فجاز لهم أن يشهدوا عليه تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٢٠/٩] يسمع كما لو ضمن الدرك أو تقاضى الثمن؛ لأنه تلبيس محض، وحضوره عند البيع وتركه فيما يصنع إقرار منه بأنه ملك البائع، وأن لا حق له في المبيع، وجعل سكوته في هذه الحالة كالإفصاح بالإقرار قطعا للإضرار بالناس، و لم يعين الشيخ القريب بل أطلقه وفي "الفتاوى" لأبي الليث عينه فقال لو باع عقارا وابنه أو امرأته حاضر يعلم به، وتصرف المشتري فيه زمانا، ثم ادعى الابن أنه ملكه، ولم يكن ملك أبيه وقت البيع، اتفق مشايخنا على أنه لا تسمع مثل هذه الدعوى؛ لأن حضوره عند البيع وتركه فيما يصنع إقرار منه بأنه ملك البائع، وأنه لا حق له في المبيع، وجعل سكوته في هذه الحالة كالإفصاح بالإقرار قطعا للأطماع الفاسدة لأهل العصر في الإضرار بالناس، وتقييد القريب يقتضي جواز ذلك مع الغريب قال في "الخلاصة: والأصح أنها تسمع من القريب وغيره.
Book of the Hermaphrodite. Miscellaneous issues. ... He sold a female donkey, its foal is not included in the sale. A disputed property is not removed from the hand of its possessor unless the plaintiff proves [the defendant's possession]. A property not within the judge's jurisdiction: his judgment therein is not valid. If a judge passes judgment in a case based on evidence, then says: I have retracted my judgment, or it has become otherwise apparent to me, or I have been deceived by the witnesses, or I have annulled my judgment, it is not considered. ... And similar things are not considered, and the judgment is effective if it was after a valid claim and upright testimony. He hid some people, then asked a man about something, and he admitted it while they saw him and heard his speech, and he did not see them – their testimony is valid. But if they heard his speech and did not see him, their testimony is not valid. ... He sold a property while some of his relatives were present, knowing of the sale, then he claimed [ownership] – his claim is not heard.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage is a collection of independent rulings from the Book of the Hermaphrodite in Kanz al-Daqa'iq, supplemented by commentary from later works. The first ruling states that when selling a female donkey, the foal is not automatically included; it must be explicitly mentioned. The second ruling addresses property disputes: the plaintiff must prove that the defendant is in possession, because possession is necessary for a valid claim. Unlike movable property, possession of real estate is not obvious and must be established by evidence or judicial notice. The third ruling concerns jurisdiction: a judge cannot adjudicate over property outside his territorial authority, though later authorities like al-Tanwir consider the correct opinion to be that he can, and this is the fatwa. The fourth ruling discusses when a judge may revoke his own judgment: if it was based on evidence, he cannot retract it arbitrarily because the right of the successful party has attached; but if he judged based on his own knowledge, contrary to his school, or if error appears, he may revoke. The fifth ruling deals with hidden witnesses: if they see and hear the admission, they may testify; if they only hear without seeing, testimony is not allowed due to the possibility of mistaken identity, unless circumstances ensure certainty. The final ruling states that if a relative is present at a sale and remains silent, he cannot later claim ownership of the property; his silence is deemed an admission of the seller's ownership. Some scholars limit this to relatives, while others extend it to any person. All rulings are based on principles of avoiding harm and ensuring certainty in legal matters.

Key Terms
ولاية القاضي (wilāyat al-qāḍī): Territorial jurisdiction of a judge
مصر (miṣr): Capital city or principal city of a region

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view, what is the ruling on a judge's judgment over property outside his jurisdiction?
A) It is invalid for all property.
B) It is valid only for movable property.
C) It is valid for both movables and immovables, but must be executed by the local judge.
D) It is invalid unless the judge is accompanied by the caliph.

Key Takeaway
The later Hanafi position allows a judge to adjudicate over property outside his district, though execution is handled locally.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Judge's Revocation of Judgment
A ruling on the possibility of a judge revoking his own judgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a judge may revoke his own judgment and explain why it is generally not allowed.

Core Idea
A valid judgment based on evidence cannot be revoked once rights have attached.

When can a judge revoke his own ruling? The passage addresses this: if the judgment was based on evidence (bayyina), the judge cannot retract it simply because he changes his mind or discovers deception, because the successful party's right has attached. However, if the judgment was based on the judge's own knowledge, contrary to his school, or if an error appears, he may revoke.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A judge passes a judgment based on evidence (bayyina). Later he says: 'I retract,' 'it appears otherwise,' 'I was deceived,' or 'I annul.'
2
State the general rule
Such statements are not considered; the judgment remains effective.
Because the right of the successful party has attached.
3
Identify the exceptions
If the judge judged based on his own knowledge, contrary to his madhhab, or if an error appears, he may revoke.
The passage mentions these three exceptions.
4
Apply the ruling
If the judge admits deception by witnesses, but the judgment was based on evidence, he cannot revoke because the witnesses' testimony was accepted by the court.

كتاب الخنثى
مسائل شتی
ما دمت، ببخاری، فخرج منها ورجع وفعل لا يحنث باع أتانا لا يدخل جحشها في البيع. والعقار المتنازع فيه لا يخرج من يد ذي اليد ما لم يبرهن المدعي. عقار لا في ولاية القاضي لا يصح قضاؤه فيه. إذا قضى القاضي في حادثة ببينة، ثم قال: رجعت عن قضائي، أو بدا لي غير ذلك، أو وقعت في تلبيس الشهود، أو أبطلت حكمي، قال قال من قال وهو ظاهر، أقول: وهذه المسألة وكذا التي بعدها أعني: قوله باع أتانا إلخ مذكورتان في النسخ المطبوعة. الكنز الموجودة عندي لكن لم يأخذهما أحد من الشراح مثل الطائي وملا مسكين وصاحب "التكملة"، وأما العيني فلم تذكر فيه هاتان المسألتان على ما نقله في حاشية الكنز المطبوع في "بمب"، وذكرهما في حاشية الكنز المطبوع بمطبع الأحمدي، و لم أظفر على أصل نسخة العيني لأنظر ما فيه فليتنبه له وعلى كل حال فالمراد ظاهر.
أتانا باع إلخ: أي إن باع رجل أتانا لا يدخل ولدها المنفصل في البيع وهو ظاهر أيضا، وقد ذكرت ما يتعلق بهذه المسألة في الصفحة الماضية عند قوله: إن فعلت كذا، فليذكر ما لم يبرهن المدعي أي إذا ادعى عقارا لا يكتفي بذكر المدعي أنه في يد المدعى عليه حتى تصح دعواه، بل لابد أن يبرهن أنه في يده، أو يعلم القاضي بذلك في الصحيح؛ لأن يد المدعى عليه لابد منه لتصح الدعوى عليه، وهو شرط فيها ويحتمل أن يكون في يد غيره، فبإقامة البينة تنفي تهمة المواضعة فيقضي القاضي عليه بإخراجه من يده لتحقق يده بخلاف المنقول؛ لأن اليد فيه مشاهدة، فلا يحتاج إلى إثباتها بالبينة، فإن قيل: هذه مكررة من قوله في كتاب الدعوى: "ولا تثبت اليد في العقار بتصادقهما بل ببينة أو إعلام، قاض بخلاف المنقول؟ قلنا لا تكرار؛ لأن تلك بالنظر إلى ثبوت اليد، وهذه بالنظر إلى أن القاضي هل يملك إخراجها من ذي اليد؟ تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤١٩/٩] يصح قضاؤه إلخ: أي إذا كان عقار متنازع فيه وليس في ولاية القاضي لا يصح قضاؤه في ذلك العقار؛ لأنه لا ولاية له في ذلك المكان، وقد اختلف المشايخ هل يعتبر المكان أو الأهل؟ فقيل: يعتبر المكان، وقيل: الأهل، حتى لا ينفذ قضاؤه في غير ذلك المكان على قول من اعتبر المكان، ولا في غير ذلك الأهل على قول من اعتبر الأهل، لا وإن خرج القاضي مع الخليفة من المصر، قضى وإن خرج وحده لم يجز قضاؤه. رمز الحقائق: ٥٠٦/٢] قال في الفتح واعلم أن ما جزم به في "الكنز" و"الملتقى" خلاف الصحيح، قال في "التنوير" وشرحه: عقار لا في ولاية القاضي، يصح قضاؤه فيه كمنقول هو الصحيح، وتقدم في القضاء أن المصر ليس بشرط فيه، به يفتى، ويكتب بالحكم القاضي تلك الناحية ليأمره بالتسليم. ببينة إلخ: تقييده بالبينة يشير إلى الاحتراز عما لو قضى بعلمه أو بخلاف مذهبه أو ظهر خطؤه، ففي هذه الثلاث يجوز له الرجوع، وفي "التنوير" وشرحه قال الشهود قضيت وأنكر القاضي، فالقول له، به يفتى، خلافا لمحمد ما لم ينفذه قاض آخر، فحينئذ يكون القول قوله؛ لوجود قضاء الثاني. (فتح)
ونحو ذلك، لا يعتبر، والقضاء ماض إن كان بعد دعوى صحيحة وشهادة مستقيمة. خبأ قوما، ثم سأل رجلا عن شيء، فأقر به، وهم يرونه ويسمعون كلامه، وهو لا يراهم جازت شهادتهم، وإن سمعوا كلامه ولم يروه لا باع عقارا وبعض أقاربه حاضر يعلم البيع ثم ادعى، لا يسمع دعواه. ونحو ذلك: نحو أن يقول: رجعت عن حكمي أو فسخته ونحوها لا يعتبر أي قول القاضي في هذه الصور؛ لتعلق حق الغير به، وهو المدعي. (فتح) والقضاء ماض إلخ لأن رأيه الأول قد ترجح بالقضاء، فلا ينقض باجتهاد مثله، ولا يملك الرجوع عنه، ولا إبطاله؛ لأنه تعلق به حق الغير، وهو المدعي، ألا ترى أن الشهادة لما اتصلت بالقضاء لا يصح رجوعه، ولا يملك إبطالها لما ذكرنا فكذا القضاء تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٢٠/٩] بعد دعوى صحيحة إلخ وهي ما يتعلق بها أحكامها من إحضار الخصم والمطالبة بالجواب والإتيان بالبينة. (ملا مسكين) شهادة مستقيمة وهي شهادة عدول إذا أجمعت شرائط الصحة احتراز عما إذا قال ذلك بعد دعوى فاسدة أو شهادة غير مستقيمة، وصورة الدعوى الفاسدة إذا ادعى محدودا و لم يبين أنه كرم أو أرض، والشهود شهدوا كذلك ملا) (مسكين رجلا آخر عن شيء مثل دينا له. جازت شهادتهم إلخ: أي شهادة القوم الذين خبأهم على ذلك الرجل بالإقرار؛ لأن الإقرار موجب بنفسه، وقد علموه، وهو أي العلم يكفي في أداء الشهادة، قال الله تعالى: ﴿إِلَّا مَنْ شَهِدَ بِالْحَقِّ وَهُمْ يَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ (الزخرف:٨٦) وقال عليه: "إذا علمت مثل الشمس فاشهد وإلا فدع تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤۲۰/۹] لا : يعني وإن سمع القوم الذين خبأهم كلام ذلك الرجل المسئول و لم يروه، لا تجوز شهادتهم عليه؛ لأن النغمة تشبه النغمة، فيحتمل أن يكون المقر، غيره فلا يجوز لهم أن يشهدوا عليه مع الاحتمال، إلا إذا كانوا دخلوا البيت وعلموا أنه ليس فيه أحد سواهم، ثم جلسوا على الباب وليس للبيت مسلك غيره، ثم دخل رجل، فسمعوا إقرار الداخل، و لم يروه وقت الإقرار؛ لأن العلم حصل لهم في هذه الصورة، فجاز لهم أن يشهدوا عليه تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٢٠/٩] يسمع كما لو ضمن الدرك أو تقاضى الثمن؛ لأنه تلبيس محض، وحضوره عند البيع وتركه فيما يصنع إقرار منه بأنه ملك البائع، وأن لا حق له في المبيع، وجعل سكوته في هذه الحالة كالإفصاح بالإقرار قطعا للإضرار بالناس، و لم يعين الشيخ القريب بل أطلقه وفي "الفتاوى" لأبي الليث عينه فقال لو باع عقارا وابنه أو امرأته حاضر يعلم به، وتصرف المشتري فيه زمانا، ثم ادعى الابن أنه ملكه، ولم يكن ملك أبيه وقت البيع، اتفق مشايخنا على أنه لا تسمع مثل هذه الدعوى؛ لأن حضوره عند البيع وتركه فيما يصنع إقرار منه بأنه ملك البائع، وأنه لا حق له في المبيع، وجعل سكوته في هذه الحالة كالإفصاح بالإقرار قطعا للأطماع الفاسدة لأهل العصر في الإضرار بالناس، وتقييد القريب يقتضي جواز ذلك مع الغريب قال في "الخلاصة: والأصح أنها تسمع من القريب وغيره.
Book of the Hermaphrodite. Miscellaneous issues. ... He sold a female donkey, its foal is not included in the sale. A disputed property is not removed from the hand of its possessor unless the plaintiff proves [the defendant's possession]. A property not within the judge's jurisdiction: his judgment therein is not valid. If a judge passes judgment in a case based on evidence, then says: I have retracted my judgment, or it has become otherwise apparent to me, or I have been deceived by the witnesses, or I have annulled my judgment, it is not considered. ... And similar things are not considered, and the judgment is effective if it was after a valid claim and upright testimony. He hid some people, then asked a man about something, and he admitted it while they saw him and heard his speech, and he did not see them – their testimony is valid. But if they heard his speech and did not see him, their testimony is not valid. ... He sold a property while some of his relatives were present, knowing of the sale, then he claimed [ownership] – his claim is not heard.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage is a collection of independent rulings from the Book of the Hermaphrodite in Kanz al-Daqa'iq, supplemented by commentary from later works. The first ruling states that when selling a female donkey, the foal is not automatically included; it must be explicitly mentioned. The second ruling addresses property disputes: the plaintiff must prove that the defendant is in possession, because possession is necessary for a valid claim. Unlike movable property, possession of real estate is not obvious and must be established by evidence or judicial notice. The third ruling concerns jurisdiction: a judge cannot adjudicate over property outside his territorial authority, though later authorities like al-Tanwir consider the correct opinion to be that he can, and this is the fatwa. The fourth ruling discusses when a judge may revoke his own judgment: if it was based on evidence, he cannot retract it arbitrarily because the right of the successful party has attached; but if he judged based on his own knowledge, contrary to his school, or if error appears, he may revoke. The fifth ruling deals with hidden witnesses: if they see and hear the admission, they may testify; if they only hear without seeing, testimony is not allowed due to the possibility of mistaken identity, unless circumstances ensure certainty. The final ruling states that if a relative is present at a sale and remains silent, he cannot later claim ownership of the property; his silence is deemed an admission of the seller's ownership. Some scholars limit this to relatives, while others extend it to any person. All rulings are based on principles of avoiding harm and ensuring certainty in legal matters.

Key Terms
قضى بعلمه (qaḍā bi-‘ilmihi): Judged based on his own personal knowledge
بينة (bayyina): Evidence, usually witnesses

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following cases may a judge revoke his own judgment according to the passage?
A) If he judged based on evidence and later discovers the witnesses were lying.
B) If he judged based on his own knowledge and later changes his mind.
C) If the losing party requests a retrial.
D) If he judged based on evidence and the winning party agrees to revocation.

Key Takeaway
A judge's judgment based on evidence is final and cannot be unilaterally revoked, except in three specific cases.

Testimony of Hidden Witnesses
A ruling on admissibility of testimony from hidden witnesses who heard an admission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for when hidden witnesses can testify based on hearing an admission, and identify the condition of visual identification.

Core Idea
Hearing alone is insufficient for testimony; witness must see the person to confirm identity.

The passage addresses a scenario where a person hides witnesses to hear an admission. If the witnesses both see and hear the person admit, they may testify. But if they only hear the voice without seeing, their testimony is not accepted due to the possibility of mistaken identity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person hides some people (witnesses), then asks a man about something, and the man admits it.
2
Condition 1: witnesses see and hear
If the witnesses see the person and hear his speech, their testimony is valid.
Because they have certain knowledge of identity and content.
3
Condition 2: hear only
If they hear but do not see, testimony is invalid due to possibility of mistaken identity.
Voices can be similar.
4
Exception: certainty despite not seeing
If they entered the house and knew no one else was there, then sat at the only exit and heard a man from inside, they may testify because certainty is attained.
The passage mentions this scenario.

Source Text

كتاب الخنثى
مسائل شتی
ما دمت، ببخاری، فخرج منها ورجع وفعل لا يحنث باع أتانا لا يدخل جحشها في البيع. والعقار المتنازع فيه لا يخرج من يد ذي اليد ما لم يبرهن المدعي. عقار لا في ولاية القاضي لا يصح قضاؤه فيه. إذا قضى القاضي في حادثة ببينة، ثم قال: رجعت عن قضائي، أو بدا لي غير ذلك، أو وقعت في تلبيس الشهود، أو أبطلت حكمي، قال قال من قال وهو ظاهر، أقول: وهذه المسألة وكذا التي بعدها أعني: قوله باع أتانا إلخ مذكورتان في النسخ المطبوعة. الكنز الموجودة عندي لكن لم يأخذهما أحد من الشراح مثل الطائي وملا مسكين وصاحب "التكملة"، وأما العيني فلم تذكر فيه هاتان المسألتان على ما نقله في حاشية الكنز المطبوع في "بمب"، وذكرهما في حاشية الكنز المطبوع بمطبع الأحمدي، و لم أظفر على أصل نسخة العيني لأنظر ما فيه فليتنبه له وعلى كل حال فالمراد ظاهر.
أتانا باع إلخ: أي إن باع رجل أتانا لا يدخل ولدها المنفصل في البيع وهو ظاهر أيضا، وقد ذكرت ما يتعلق بهذه المسألة في الصفحة الماضية عند قوله: إن فعلت كذا، فليذكر ما لم يبرهن المدعي أي إذا ادعى عقارا لا يكتفي بذكر المدعي أنه في يد المدعى عليه حتى تصح دعواه، بل لابد أن يبرهن أنه في يده، أو يعلم القاضي بذلك في الصحيح؛ لأن يد المدعى عليه لابد منه لتصح الدعوى عليه، وهو شرط فيها ويحتمل أن يكون في يد غيره، فبإقامة البينة تنفي تهمة المواضعة فيقضي القاضي عليه بإخراجه من يده لتحقق يده بخلاف المنقول؛ لأن اليد فيه مشاهدة، فلا يحتاج إلى إثباتها بالبينة، فإن قيل: هذه مكررة من قوله في كتاب الدعوى: "ولا تثبت اليد في العقار بتصادقهما بل ببينة أو إعلام، قاض بخلاف المنقول؟ قلنا لا تكرار؛ لأن تلك بالنظر إلى ثبوت اليد، وهذه بالنظر إلى أن القاضي هل يملك إخراجها من ذي اليد؟ تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤١٩/٩] يصح قضاؤه إلخ: أي إذا كان عقار متنازع فيه وليس في ولاية القاضي لا يصح قضاؤه في ذلك العقار؛ لأنه لا ولاية له في ذلك المكان، وقد اختلف المشايخ هل يعتبر المكان أو الأهل؟ فقيل: يعتبر المكان، وقيل: الأهل، حتى لا ينفذ قضاؤه في غير ذلك المكان على قول من اعتبر المكان، ولا في غير ذلك الأهل على قول من اعتبر الأهل، لا وإن خرج القاضي مع الخليفة من المصر، قضى وإن خرج وحده لم يجز قضاؤه. رمز الحقائق: ٥٠٦/٢] قال في الفتح واعلم أن ما جزم به في "الكنز" و"الملتقى" خلاف الصحيح، قال في "التنوير" وشرحه: عقار لا في ولاية القاضي، يصح قضاؤه فيه كمنقول هو الصحيح، وتقدم في القضاء أن المصر ليس بشرط فيه، به يفتى، ويكتب بالحكم القاضي تلك الناحية ليأمره بالتسليم. ببينة إلخ: تقييده بالبينة يشير إلى الاحتراز عما لو قضى بعلمه أو بخلاف مذهبه أو ظهر خطؤه، ففي هذه الثلاث يجوز له الرجوع، وفي "التنوير" وشرحه قال الشهود قضيت وأنكر القاضي، فالقول له، به يفتى، خلافا لمحمد ما لم ينفذه قاض آخر، فحينئذ يكون القول قوله؛ لوجود قضاء الثاني. Book of the Hermaphrodite. Miscellaneous issues. ... He sold a female donkey, its foal is not included in the sale. A disputed property is not removed from the hand of its possessor unless the plaintiff proves [the defendant's possession]. A property not within the judge's jurisdiction: his judgment therein is not valid. If a judge passes judgment in a case based on evidence, then says: I have retracted my judgment, or it has become otherwise apparent to me, or I have been deceived by the witnesses, or I have annulled my judgment, it is not considered. ... And similar things are not considered, and the judgment is effective if it was after a valid claim and upright testimony. He hid some people, then asked a man about something, and he admitted it while they saw him and heard his speech, and he did not see them – their testimony is valid. But if they heard his speech and did not see him, their testimony is not valid. ... He sold a property while some of his relatives were present, knowing of the sale, then he claimed [ownership] – his claim is not heard.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage is a collection of independent rulings from the Book of the Hermaphrodite in Kanz al-Daqa'iq, supplemented by commentary from later works. The first ruling states that when selling a female donkey, the foal is not automatically included; it must be explicitly mentioned. The second ruling addresses property disputes: the plaintiff must prove that the defendant is in possession, because possession is necessary for a valid claim. Unlike movable property, possession of real estate is not obvious and must be established by evidence or judicial notice. The third ruling concerns jurisdiction: a judge cannot adjudicate over property outside his territorial authority, though later authorities like al-Tanwir consider the correct opinion to be that he can, and this is the fatwa. The fourth ruling discusses when a judge may revoke his own judgment: if it was based on evidence, he cannot retract it arbitrarily because the right of the successful party has attached; but if he judged based on his own knowledge, contrary to his school, or if error appears, he may revoke. The fifth ruling deals with hidden witnesses: if they see and hear the admission, they may testify; if they only hear without seeing, testimony is not allowed due to the possibility of mistaken identity, unless circumstances ensure certainty. The final ruling states that if a relative is present at a sale and remains silent, he cannot later claim ownership of the property; his silence is deemed an admission of the seller's ownership. Some scholars limit this to relatives, while others extend it to any person. All rulings are based on principles of avoiding harm and ensuring certainty in legal matters.

Key Terms
خبأ (khaba'a): Hid, concealed
نغمة (naghmatun): Tone, voice

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition may hidden witnesses testify based solely on hearing an admission?
A) Always, if they heard clearly.
B) Only if they also saw the speaker.
C) Only if the admission was made in writing.
D) Only if they are relatives of the confessor.

Key Takeaway
Testimony based on hearing alone is invalid due to potential mistaken identity; visual confirmation or circumstantial certainty is required.

Silence of Relative at Sale as Implied Admission
A ruling on the legal effect of a relative's silence at a sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a close relative who is present at a sale and remains silent cannot later claim ownership of the property.

Core Idea
Silence of a relative at a sale is deemed an admission of the seller's ownership.

This ruling deals with a scenario where a relative is present when a property is sold and does not object. Later, he claims the property is his. The Hanafi position is that his silence is treated as an admission that the seller was the owner, and his claim is not heard. This prevents fraudulent claims after the fact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person sells a piece of property (real estate) while some of his relatives are present and aware of the sale. Later, a relative claims that property belongs to him.
2
State the ruling
The relative's claim is not heard (lā yusma' da'wāhu).
Because his silence at the sale is considered an implicit admission of the seller's ownership.
3
Understand the rationale
If the relative had a right, he would have objected. His silence is treated as an acknowledgment (iqrar) to prevent harm (dharar) to people.
The text says: 'His silence in this situation is like openly admitting.'
4
Know the scope
Some scholars (like Abu al-Layth) specify this applies only to close relatives (like son/father/spouse), but the general text says 'some of his relatives' without restriction.
According to al-Khulasah, the claim is not heard even from a non-relative, but the more common view is for relatives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الخنثى
مسائل شتی
ما دمت، ببخاری، فخرج منها ورجع وفعل لا يحنث باع أتانا لا يدخل جحشها في البيع. والعقار المتنازع فيه لا يخرج من يد ذي اليد ما لم يبرهن المدعي. عقار لا في ولاية القاضي لا يصح قضاؤه فيه. إذا قضى القاضي في حادثة ببينة، ثم قال: رجعت عن قضائي، أو بدا لي غير ذلك، أو وقعت في تلبيس الشهود، أو أبطلت حكمي، قال قال من قال وهو ظاهر، أقول: وهذه المسألة وكذا التي بعدها أعني: قوله باع أتانا إلخ مذكورتان في النسخ المطبوعة. الكنز الموجودة عندي لكن لم يأخذهما أحد من الشراح مثل الطائي وملا مسكين وصاحب "التكملة"، وأما العيني فلم تذكر فيه هاتان المسألتان على ما نقله في حاشية الكنز المطبوع في "بمب"، وذكرهما في حاشية الكنز المطبوع بمطبع الأحمدي، و لم أظفر على أصل نسخة العيني لأنظر ما فيه فليتنبه له وعلى كل حال فالمراد ظاهر.
أتانا باع إلخ: أي إن باع رجل أتانا لا يدخل ولدها المنفصل في البيع وهو ظاهر أيضا، وقد ذكرت ما يتعلق بهذه المسألة في الصفحة الماضية عند قوله: إن فعلت كذا، فليذكر ما لم يبرهن المدعي أي إذا ادعى عقارا لا يكتفي بذكر المدعي أنه في يد المدعى عليه حتى تصح دعواه، بل لابد أن يبرهن أنه في يده، أو يعلم القاضي بذلك في الصحيح؛ لأن يد المدعى عليه لابد منه لتصح الدعوى عليه، وهو شرط فيها ويحتمل أن يكون في يد غيره، فبإقامة البينة تنفي تهمة المواضعة فيقضي القاضي عليه بإخراجه من يده لتحقق يده بخلاف المنقول؛ لأن اليد فيه مشاهدة، فلا يحتاج إلى إثباتها بالبينة، فإن قيل: هذه مكررة من قوله في كتاب الدعوى: "ولا تثبت اليد في العقار بتصادقهما بل ببينة أو إعلام، قاض بخلاف المنقول؟ قلنا لا تكرار؛ لأن تلك بالنظر إلى ثبوت اليد، وهذه بالنظر إلى أن القاضي هل يملك إخراجها من ذي اليد؟ تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤١٩/٩] يصح قضاؤه إلخ: أي إذا كان عقار متنازع فيه وليس في ولاية القاضي لا يصح قضاؤه في ذلك العقار؛ لأنه لا ولاية له في ذلك المكان، وقد اختلف المشايخ هل يعتبر المكان أو الأهل؟ فقيل: يعتبر المكان، وقيل: الأهل، حتى لا ينفذ قضاؤه في غير ذلك المكان على قول من اعتبر المكان، ولا في غير ذلك الأهل على قول من اعتبر الأهل، لا وإن خرج القاضي مع الخليفة من المصر، قضى وإن خرج وحده لم يجز قضاؤه. رمز الحقائق: ٥٠٦/٢] قال في الفتح واعلم أن ما جزم به في "الكنز" و"الملتقى" خلاف الصحيح، قال في "التنوير" وشرحه: عقار لا في ولاية القاضي، يصح قضاؤه فيه كمنقول هو الصحيح، وتقدم في القضاء أن المصر ليس بشرط فيه، به يفتى، ويكتب بالحكم القاضي تلك الناحية ليأمره بالتسليم. ببينة إلخ: تقييده بالبينة يشير إلى الاحتراز عما لو قضى بعلمه أو بخلاف مذهبه أو ظهر خطؤه، ففي هذه الثلاث يجوز له الرجوع، وفي "التنوير" وشرحه قال الشهود قضيت وأنكر القاضي، فالقول له، به يفتى، خلافا لمحمد ما لم ينفذه قاض آخر، فحينئذ يكون القول قوله؛ لوجود قضاء الثاني. (فتح)
ونحو ذلك، لا يعتبر، والقضاء ماض إن كان بعد دعوى صحيحة وشهادة مستقيمة. خبأ قوما، ثم سأل رجلا عن شيء، فأقر به، وهم يرونه ويسمعون كلامه، وهو لا يراهم جازت شهادتهم، وإن سمعوا كلامه ولم يروه لا باع عقارا وبعض أقاربه حاضر يعلم البيع ثم ادعى، لا يسمع دعواه. ونحو ذلك: نحو أن يقول: رجعت عن حكمي أو فسخته ونحوها لا يعتبر أي قول القاضي في هذه الصور؛ لتعلق حق الغير به، وهو المدعي. (فتح) والقضاء ماض إلخ لأن رأيه الأول قد ترجح بالقضاء، فلا ينقض باجتهاد مثله، ولا يملك الرجوع عنه، ولا إبطاله؛ لأنه تعلق به حق الغير، وهو المدعي، ألا ترى أن الشهادة لما اتصلت بالقضاء لا يصح رجوعه، ولا يملك إبطالها لما ذكرنا فكذا القضاء تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٢٠/٩] بعد دعوى صحيحة إلخ وهي ما يتعلق بها أحكامها من إحضار الخصم والمطالبة بالجواب والإتيان بالبينة. (ملا مسكين) شهادة مستقيمة وهي شهادة عدول إذا أجمعت شرائط الصحة احتراز عما إذا قال ذلك بعد دعوى فاسدة أو شهادة غير مستقيمة، وصورة الدعوى الفاسدة إذا ادعى محدودا و لم يبين أنه كرم أو أرض، والشهود شهدوا كذلك ملا) (مسكين رجلا آخر عن شيء مثل دينا له. جازت شهادتهم إلخ: أي شهادة القوم الذين خبأهم على ذلك الرجل بالإقرار؛ لأن الإقرار موجب بنفسه، وقد علموه، وهو أي العلم يكفي في أداء الشهادة، قال الله تعالى: ﴿إِلَّا مَنْ شَهِدَ بِالْحَقِّ وَهُمْ يَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ (الزخرف:٨٦) وقال عليه: "إذا علمت مثل الشمس فاشهد وإلا فدع تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤۲۰/۹] لا : يعني وإن سمع القوم الذين خبأهم كلام ذلك الرجل المسئول و لم يروه، لا تجوز شهادتهم عليه؛ لأن النغمة تشبه النغمة، فيحتمل أن يكون المقر، غيره فلا يجوز لهم أن يشهدوا عليه مع الاحتمال، إلا إذا كانوا دخلوا البيت وعلموا أنه ليس فيه أحد سواهم، ثم جلسوا على الباب وليس للبيت مسلك غيره، ثم دخل رجل، فسمعوا إقرار الداخل، و لم يروه وقت الإقرار؛ لأن العلم حصل لهم في هذه الصورة، فجاز لهم أن يشهدوا عليه تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٢٠/٩] يسمع كما لو ضمن الدرك أو تقاضى الثمن؛ لأنه تلبيس محض، وحضوره عند البيع وتركه فيما يصنع إقرار منه بأنه ملك البائع، وأن لا حق له في المبيع، وجعل سكوته في هذه الحالة كالإفصاح بالإقرار قطعا للإضرار بالناس، و لم يعين الشيخ القريب بل أطلقه وفي "الفتاوى" لأبي الليث عينه فقال لو باع عقارا وابنه أو امرأته حاضر يعلم به، وتصرف المشتري فيه زمانا، ثم ادعى الابن أنه ملكه، ولم يكن ملك أبيه وقت البيع، اتفق مشايخنا على أنه لا تسمع مثل هذه الدعوى؛ لأن حضوره عند البيع وتركه فيما يصنع إقرار منه بأنه ملك البائع، وأنه لا حق له في المبيع، وجعل سكوته في هذه الحالة كالإفصاح بالإقرار قطعا للأطماع الفاسدة لأهل العصر في الإضرار بالناس، وتقييد القريب يقتضي جواز ذلك مع الغريب قال في "الخلاصة: والأصح أنها تسمع من القريب وغيره.
Book of the Hermaphrodite. Miscellaneous issues. ... He sold a female donkey, its foal is not included in the sale. A disputed property is not removed from the hand of its possessor unless the plaintiff proves [the defendant's possession]. A property not within the judge's jurisdiction: his judgment therein is not valid. If a judge passes judgment in a case based on evidence, then says: I have retracted my judgment, or it has become otherwise apparent to me, or I have been deceived by the witnesses, or I have annulled my judgment, it is not considered. ... And similar things are not considered, and the judgment is effective if it was after a valid claim and upright testimony. He hid some people, then asked a man about something, and he admitted it while they saw him and heard his speech, and he did not see them – their testimony is valid. But if they heard his speech and did not see him, their testimony is not valid. ... He sold a property while some of his relatives were present, knowing of the sale, then he claimed [ownership] – his claim is not heard.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage is a collection of independent rulings from the Book of the Hermaphrodite in Kanz al-Daqa'iq, supplemented by commentary from later works. The first ruling states that when selling a female donkey, the foal is not automatically included; it must be explicitly mentioned. The second ruling addresses property disputes: the plaintiff must prove that the defendant is in possession, because possession is necessary for a valid claim. Unlike movable property, possession of real estate is not obvious and must be established by evidence or judicial notice. The third ruling concerns jurisdiction: a judge cannot adjudicate over property outside his territorial authority, though later authorities like al-Tanwir consider the correct opinion to be that he can, and this is the fatwa. The fourth ruling discusses when a judge may revoke his own judgment: if it was based on evidence, he cannot retract it arbitrarily because the right of the successful party has attached; but if he judged based on his own knowledge, contrary to his school, or if error appears, he may revoke. The fifth ruling deals with hidden witnesses: if they see and hear the admission, they may testify; if they only hear without seeing, testimony is not allowed due to the possibility of mistaken identity, unless circumstances ensure certainty. The final ruling states that if a relative is present at a sale and remains silent, he cannot later claim ownership of the property; his silence is deemed an admission of the seller's ownership. Some scholars limit this to relatives, while others extend it to any person. All rulings are based on principles of avoiding harm and ensuring certainty in legal matters.

Key Terms
تلبيس (talbīs): Deception, fraud
إقرار (iqrār): Admission, acknowledgment

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal effect of a relative's silence when present at a sale?
A) It has no effect; the relative can still claim later.
B) It is treated as an admission that the seller owns the property.
C) It is considered a request for more information.
D) It voids the sale.

Key Takeaway
Silence of a relative present at a sale is a legally binding implied admission that bars later ownership claims.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Silence at Sale Bars Later Claim
Ruling with expansion on a claim-barring rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a relative present at a sale cannot later claim ownership, explain the rationale (talil) of treating silence as acknowledgment, and distinguish the views on whether this applies to strangers.

Core Idea
Silence at sale is implicit acknowledgment; later claim is fraud.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling designed to prevent fraud and protect transactions. If a person is present when a property is sold, and does not object, they cannot later sue the buyer claiming ownership. The law treats their silence as an acknowledgment that the seller owned the property. This rule is based on istihsan and blocking harm. There is an important intra-Hanafi difference on whether the rule applies only to relatives or to everyone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the core legal outcome: the claim is not heard (لا تسمع الدعوى). Determine what triggers this ruling: the claimant was present at the sale and remained silent.
2
Understand the rationale (talil)
Analyze why silence is treated as acknowledgment (إقرار). The text says it is 'pure dissimulation' (تلبيس محض) and that the law 'cuts off harm to people' (قطعا للإضرار بالناس). Identify the maslaha (public interest) behind the rule.
This is a form of istihsan based on blocking evil (sadd al-dhara'i).
3
Trace the intra-madhhab dispute
Note that some early authorities (e.g., Abu al-Layth) restricted the rule to close relatives (son, wife), while others (including al-Khulasa) extended it to strangers. Determine the mufta bihi: the stronger view is that it applies to both.
The dispute hinges on whether the qarina (circumstance) of presence alone is sufficient, or requires kinship.
4
Apply to a new scenario
Given a hypothetical: 'A man's neighbor is present when the man sells a car. The neighbor later claims the car was his.' Decide whether the claim is heard, and explain using the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يسمع كما لو ضمن الدرك أو تقاضى الثمن؛ لأنه تلبيس محض، وحضوره عند البيع وتركه فيما يصنع إقرار منه بأنه ملك البائع، وأن لا حق له في المبيع، وجعل سكوته في هذه الحالة كالإفصاح بالإقرار قطعا للإضرار بالناس، و لم يعين الشيخ القريب بل أطلقه وفي "الفتاوى" لأبي الليث عينه فقال لو باع عقارا وابنه أو امرأته حاضر يعلم به، وتصرف المشتري فيه زمانا، ثم ادعى الابن أنه ملكه، ولم يكن ملك أبيه وقت البيع، اتفق مشايخنا على أنه لا تسمع مثل هذه الدعوى؛ لأن حضوره عند البيع وتركه فيما يصنع إقرار منه بأنه ملك البائع، وأنه لا حق له في المبيع، وجعل سكوته في هذه الحالة كالإفصاح بالإقرار قطعا للأطماع الفاسدة لأهل العصر في الإضرار بالناس، وتقييد القريب يقتضي جواز ذلك مع الغريب قال في "الخلاصة : والأصح أنها تسمع من القريب وغيره.
It is heard? rather it is not heard, like if he guarantees the purchase price or demands payment, because it is pure dissimulation. His presence at the sale and his leaving the buyer to act is an acknowledgment from him that it is the seller's property and that he has no right in the sold item. His silence in this situation is made like explicit acknowledgment to cut off harm to people. The shaykh did not specify the relative but left it general, and in al-Fatawa of Abu al-Layth he specified it, saying: if he sold property while his son or wife was present and aware, and the buyer disposed of it for a time, then the son claimed it was his and was not his father's at the time of sale, our mashayikh agreed that such a claim is not heard because his presence at the sale and leaving the buyer to act is an acknowledgment that it is the seller's property and he has no right in it. His silence is made like explicit acknowledgment to cut off corrupt ambitions of the people of this age in harming others. Restricting it to the relative implies that it is permitted with a stranger. Al-Khulasa said: the correct view is that it is heard from both relative and stranger.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where a person is present at the sale of property owned by someone else (e.g., his father) and does not object. Later, he claims that the property was actually his. The Hanafi ruling is that such a claim is not heard because his presence and silence constitute an implicit acknowledgment that the seller owns the property and that he has no right in it. This is a measure to prevent fraud and harm. There is a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars: some specify this ruling for close relatives (like son or wife), while others generalize it. The correct view, according to al-Khulasa, is that the claim is not heard from both relative and stranger. The ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) to block evil practices.

Key Terms
تلبيس (talbīs): Deception or dissimulation; the action of the claimant who remains silent then later claims ownership.
إقرار (iqrār): Acknowledgment; here, silence is treated as implicit acknowledgment of the seller's ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason for treating silence as an acknowledgment?
A) Because the claimant is a relative.
B) To cut off harm and prevent fraud.
C) Because the claimant must explicitly state ownership.
D) Because the buyer purchased in good faith.

Key Takeaway
A person present and silent at a sale cannot later claim ownership because his silence is treated as an acknowledgment that the seller owned the property; this rule applies to both relatives and strangers according to the mufta bihi position.

Silence as Acceptance in Agency, Gift of Debt, and Waqf
Hanafi ruling that silence from the moment is acceptance, with applications and an intra-school dispute on waqf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that silence from the moment constitutes acceptance (qabul) in agency, gift of debt, and waqf, and apply it to determine the validity of these transactions.

Core Idea
Silence from the moment is acceptance by custom — a silent party becomes legally bound.

This passage introduces a fundamental Hanafi principle: silence can indicate acceptance when it occurs immediately without objection. The rule applies to agency appointments, gifts of debt to the debtor, and waqf endowments. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding waqf, which this lesson also explores.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core maxim
The passage begins with 'al-iqrar laysa sababan li al-mulk' (acknowledgment is not a cause of ownership). Understand that iqrar only confirms a pre-existing right; it does not create ownership. This sets the context for the discussion of acceptance through silence.
The maxim is a preliminary point; the main focus is on silence as acceptance.
2
Extract the rule on silence
The author states: 'silence and not refusing from his moment is evidence of acceptance customarily.' This establishes that silence, when immediate, is treated as qabul (acceptance) by custom (urf).
Immediacy is key: 'from his moment' (min sa'atihi).
3
Apply to agency
If A says 'I appointed you as agent to sell this' and B remains silent, B becomes an agent. Silence functions as acceptance, binding B to the agency.
4
Apply to gift of debt
If a creditor tells the debtor 'I gift you your debt' and the debtor remains silent, the gift is valid and the debt falls. Immediate refusal would void it. This parallels the agency rule.
The same logic applies: silence = acceptance.
5
Analyze the waqf exception
When a donor says 'I have made my land a waqf for you' and the beneficiary remains silent, the default ruling is validity. However, al-Ansari (and possibly Abu Yusuf) held that silence does not accept waqf because it is for Allah; the waqf becomes effective upon the donor's declaration alone. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
The mufta bihi is the first view (silence accepts), but the other view is noted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإقرار ليس بسبب للملك، قال الآخر : وكلتك ببيع هذا، فسكت صار وكيلا، عزل المرأة المخاطب عن الرد والقبول وكلها بطلاقها لا يملك عزلها، وكلْتُكَ بكذا على أني متى عزلتك فأنت وكيلي، أي وكل امرأته يقول في عزله عزلتك ثم عزلتك، ولو قال: كلما عزلتك فأنت وكيلي، الموكل ثم يقول عرفتك يقول: رجعت عن الوكالة المعلقة، وعزلتك عن الوكالة المنجزة. إذا أراد الموكل عزله في الإقرار ليس إلخ أي الإقرار ليس بسبب للملك، ولهذا قالوا: لو أقر لرجل بمال، والمقر له يعلم أنه كاذب في إقراره لا يحل له أخذه عن كره منه فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى، إلا أن يسلمه بطيب نفسه، فيكون تمليكا مبتدأ، كذا في "ملا "مسكين واعلم أن قوله: "الإقرار ليس بسبب للملك" قد أخذه بعض الشراح مثل ملا مسكين وصاحب "التكملة" و "الطائي" ، و لم يأخذه بعضهم مثل العيني والزيلعي ولهذا قال في "الفتح": لا وجود لهذا المتن الذي شرح عليه العيني والزيلعي، ومن أخذه فمنهم من ذکره بلا واو كما هو في المتن مثل "ملا مسكين" ومنهم من ذكره بالواو مثل صاحب "التكملة" و"الطائي" فافهم واحفظ. صار وكيلا إلخ: لأن سكوته وعدم رده من ساعته دليل القبول عادة، ونظيره هبة الدين لمن عليه الدين، فإنه إذا سكت صحت الهبة، وسقط الدين؛ لما بينا، وإن قال من ساعته: لا أقبل بطل وبقي الدين على حاله، وكذا لو قال: جعلت أرضي عليك ،وقفا فسكت ،صح ولو قال: لا أقبل بطل، وقال الأنصاري: لا يبطل؛ لأنه وقع الله تعالى، قال الزيلعي والأشبه أن يكون هذا قول أبي يوسف؛ لما عرف من أ أنه . يصير وقفا بمجرد قوله: وقفت داري. (فتح) لا يملك إلخ: أي لا يملك الزوج عزلها؛ لأنه يمين من جهته؛ لما فيه من معنى اليمين، وهو تعليق الطلاق بفعلها، ولا يصلح الرجوع عن اليمين وهو تمليك من جهتها؛ لأن الوكيل هو الذي يعمل لغيره، وهي عاملة لنفسها، فلا تكون وكيلة بخلاف الأجنبي. [ تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٢٢/٩] يقول في عزله إلخ: أي يقول الموكل في عزل الوكيل : عزلتك، ثم يقول: عزلتك ؛ لأن الوكالة يجوز تعليقها بالشرط، فيجوز تعليقها بالعزل عن الوكالة، فإذا عزله : انعزل عن الوكالة المنجزة، وتنجزت المعلقة، فصار وكيلا جديدا، ثم بالعزل الثاني انعزل عن الوكالة الثانية. (فتح) عن الوكالة المعلقة إلخ : أي يقول إذا أراد أن يعزل رجعت عن الوكالة المعلقة إلخ؛ لأنه لو عزله عن المنجزة من غير رجوع لصار وكيلا مثل ما كان ولو عزله ألف مرة؛ لأن كلمة "كلما" تقتضي تكرار الأفعال لا إلى نهاية، فلا يفيد العزل إلا بعد الرجوع، حتى لو عزله ثم رجع عن المعلقة يحتاج إلى عزل آخر؛ لأنه كلما عزله صار وكيلا، فلا يفيد الرجوع بعد ذلك عن المعلقة في حقها؛ لأنه يحتاج إلى عزل آخر بعد الرجوع، وقيل: يقول في عزله: كلما وكلتك فأنت معزول؛ لأنه كلما صار وكيلا ،انعزل فيحصل مقصوده بذلك، والأول أوجه. رمز الحقائق ٥٠٨/٢] الوكالة المنجزة إلخ اعلم أنه كانت عبارة المتن في النسخ المطبوعة هكذا: "رجعت عن الوكالة "المنجزة وهذه العبارة مع كونها مخالفة لما أثبته جميع الشراح كانت ناقصة أيضا لا تفي بالمقصود .
Acknowledgment (iqrar) is not a cause for ownership. The other said: I appointed you as agent to sell this, and he remained silent, so he became an agent. The woman being addressed is removed from reply and acceptance. He appointed her for divorce does not have the power to remove her. 'I appointed you for such-and-such on condition that whenever I remove you, you are my agent' meaning he appoints his wife, in his removal he says 'I removed you, then I removed you.' And if he said 'every time I remove you, you are my agent,' the principal then says 'I have known you' (?) he says: I have revoked the conditional agency, and I have removed you from the unconditional agency. When the principal wants to remove him, in 'acknowledgment is not a cause...' etc., i.e., acknowledgment is not a cause for ownership. For this reason they said: If he acknowledged a property to a man, and the acknowledged-to knows that he is lying in his acknowledgment, it is not permissible for him to take it against his will between him and Allah Almighty, unless he hands it over willingly, then it is a new ownership (tamlik mubtada). So in Mulla Miskin. Know that his statement 'acknowledgment is not a cause for ownership' has been taken by some commentators like Mulla Miskin and the author of al-Takmila and al-Ta'i, and some like al-Ayni and al-Zayla'i did not take it. Hence he said in al-Fath: This text does not exist in the version that al-Ayni and al-Zayla'i commented upon. And whoever took it, some mention it without a waw as in the matn like Mulla Miskin, and some mention it with a waw like the author of al-Takmila and al-Ta'i, so understand and preserve. 'He became an agent etc.': Because his silence and not refusing from his moment is evidence of acceptance customarily. Its parallel is the gift of a debt to the person who owes it, for if he remains silent, the gift is valid and the debt falls, as we explained. And if he says from his moment 'I do not accept,' it is void and the debt remains as is. Similarly, if he said 'I have made my land a waqf for you,' and he remained silent, it is valid. And if he said 'I do not accept,' it is void. And al-Ansari said: It is not void because it occurred for Allah. Al-Zayla'i said: It is more likely that this is the statement of Abu Yusuf, because it is known that he (Abu Hanifa?) 'it becomes waqf merely by his saying 'I have made my land waqf'.' (Fath) 'He does not have the power to remove her etc.': i.e., the husband does not have the power to remove her, because it is an oath from his side, due to the meaning of oath in it, and that is the suspension of divorce upon her action, and it is not proper to retract from an oath, and it is an empowerment from her side, because the agent works for someone else, while she works for herself, so she is not an agent, contrary to a third party. [Takmilat al-Bahr al-Raiq 9/422] 'He says in his removal etc.': i.e., the principal says in removing the agent: 'I removed you, then I removed you' because agency may be suspended upon a condition, so it may be suspended upon removal from agency. So when he removes him, he is removed from the unconditional agency, and the conditional one becomes unconditional, so he becomes a new agent, then by the second removal he is removed from the second agency. (Fath) 'from the conditional agency etc.': i.e., he says when he wants to remove: 'I have revoked the conditional agency...' because if he removes him from the unconditional without revocation, he would become an agent like before even if he removes him a thousand times, because the word 'kullama' requires repetition of actions ad infinitum, so the removal is not effective except after revocation. So even if he removes him then revokes the conditional, he needs another removal; because every time he removes him, he becomes an agent, so the revocation after that of the conditional does not avail with respect to it, because he needs another removal after the revocation. And it is said: He says in his removal: 'Every time I appoint you, you are removed'; because every time he becomes an agent, he is removed, thereby achieving his purpose. And the first is more appropriate. Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/508] 'The unconditional agency etc.': Know that the wording of the matn in the printed copies was: 'I revoke the unconditional agency' and this wording, despite being contrary to what all commentators established, was also deficient, not fulfilling the purpose.
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This passage from page 523 begins with the legal maxim 'al-iqrar laysa sababan li al-mulk' (acknowledgment is not a cause of ownership). It then discusses the ruling that silence can indicate acceptance in agency (wakala) and similar contexts. The maxim is explained: if a person acknowledges a property to another but the recipient knows the acknowledgment is false, it is not lawful to take it unless the acknowledger willingly hands it over, which constitutes a new act of ownership transfer (tamlik mubtada). The passage notes that different commentators recorded this maxim in varying forms. It then gives an example: if A says to B 'I appointed you as agent to sell this,' and B remains silent, he becomes an agent because silence from the moment is evidence of acceptance by custom. This is compared to the gift of a debt to the debtor: if the debtor remains silent, the gift is valid and the debt falls; if he immediately refuses, it becomes void. Similarly, for waqf, if the beneficiary remains silent upon being told 'I have made my land a waqf for you,' the waqf is valid. The last part deals with agency in divorce: a husband who says to his wife 'I appointed you for divorce' (meaning he delegates the power of divorce to her) cannot revoke that appointment because it is akin to an oath (suspension of divorce on her action). The wife acting for herself is not a true agent. The passage then discusses the complex issue of revoking agency when the agency is conditional: if the principal says 'I removed you, then I removed you,' the first removal cancels the unconditional agency and activates the conditional one, and the second removal cancels that new agency. The word 'kullama' (every time) leads to infinite cycles, so revocation requires a preliminary revocation of the condition. The commentary concludes with a textual note from Ramz al-Haqa'iq about the correct wording in the matn.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a right; here distinguished as not being a cause of ownership in itself
صمت (samt): Silence; in legal context, silence from the moment is deemed acceptance (qabul) by custom

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a creditor says to the debtor 'I forgive your debt' and the debtor remains silent immediately, what is the ruling?
A) The debt is not forgiven because silence is not acceptance
B) The debt is forgiven because silence from the moment is acceptance
C) The debt is forgiven only if the debtor later agrees in writing
D) The debt remains because the creditor cannot forgive unilaterally

Key Takeaway
Silence from the moment is acceptance by custom in agency, gift of debt, and waqf, with a minority Hanafi view on waqf that does not require acceptance at all.

Agency in Divorce and Conditional Agency Revocation
Hanafi rulings on agency in divorce and mechanics of revoking conditional agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a husband's delegation of divorce to his wife cannot be revoked, and derive the ruling on conditional agency revocation using 'kullama'.

Core Idea
Delegation of divorce to the wife is like an oath — irrevocable; and 'every time I remove you, you are my agent' creates an infinite loop requiring special revocation.

This passage deals with two nuanced agency issues: first, a husband who says to his wife 'I appoint you for divorce' gives her an irrevocable power because it is akin to a conditional oath. Second, when an agency is set up with a conditional revocation (e.g., 'every time I remove you, you become my agent again'), the principal must revoke the condition itself to break the cycle.

Guided Path
1
Understand the first case: husband's delegation of divorce
The husband says to his wife 'I appointed you for divorce' (tawkil bi al-talaq). In Hanafi law, this is not a regular agency because the wife acts for herself, not for the husband. It is a delegation that contains the meaning of an oath (yamin) — the husband suspends divorce on her action (ta'liq). Since an oath cannot be revoked, the husband cannot remove her from this power.
The key distinction: the wife is not a true agent (wakil) because she acts for her own benefit.
2
Analyze why the husband cannot revoke
The text says: 'he does not have the power to remove her, because it is an oath from his side; it contains the meaning of an oath, and it is not proper to retract from an oath.' The husband's statement is a conditional divorce (ta'liq) that gives the wife the power to divorce herself; it is not a revocable agency.
3
Examine the conditional agency case
The principal says: 'I appointed you on condition that whenever I remove you, you become my agent again.' This creates two agencies: an unconditional agency in the present, and a conditional agency that will activate upon removal.
4
Determine the correct revocation process
To terminate the cycle, the principal must first revoke the conditional agency explicitly (e.g., 'I revoke the conditional agency') and then remove the unconditional agency. If he only removes the unconditional, the conditional activates and the agent reappears.
The word 'kullama' (every time) implies infinite repetition.
5
Note an alternative method
Alternatively, the principal can say 'every time I appoint you, you are removed' (i.e., appointing automatically removes). But the first method (revoking the condition first) is more appropriate (awjah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإقرار ليس بسبب للملك، قال الآخر : وكلتك ببيع هذا، فسكت صار وكيلا، عزل المرأة المخاطب عن الرد والقبول وكلها بطلاقها لا يملك عزلها، وكلْتُكَ بكذا على أني متى عزلتك فأنت وكيلي، أي وكل امرأته يقول في عزله عزلتك ثم عزلتك، ولو قال: كلما عزلتك فأنت وكيلي، الموكل ثم يقول عرفتك يقول: رجعت عن الوكالة المعلقة، وعزلتك عن الوكالة المنجزة. إذا أراد الموكل عزله في الإقرار ليس إلخ أي الإقرار ليس بسبب للملك، ولهذا قالوا: لو أقر لرجل بمال، والمقر له يعلم أنه كاذب في إقراره لا يحل له أخذه عن كره منه فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى، إلا أن يسلمه بطيب نفسه، فيكون تمليكا مبتدأ، كذا في "ملا "مسكين واعلم أن قوله: "الإقرار ليس بسبب للملك" قد أخذه بعض الشراح مثل ملا مسكين وصاحب "التكملة" و "الطائي" ، و لم يأخذه بعضهم مثل العيني والزيلعي ولهذا قال في "الفتح": لا وجود لهذا المتن الذي شرح عليه العيني والزيلعي، ومن أخذه فمنهم من ذکره بلا واو كما هو في المتن مثل "ملا مسكين" ومنهم من ذكره بالواو مثل صاحب "التكملة" و"الطائي" فافهم واحفظ. صار وكيلا إلخ: لأن سكوته وعدم رده من ساعته دليل القبول عادة، ونظيره هبة الدين لمن عليه الدين، فإنه إذا سكت صحت الهبة، وسقط الدين؛ لما بينا، وإن قال من ساعته: لا أقبل بطل وبقي الدين على حاله، وكذا لو قال: جعلت أرضي عليك ،وقفا فسكت ،صح ولو قال: لا أقبل بطل، وقال الأنصاري: لا يبطل؛ لأنه وقع الله تعالى، قال الزيلعي والأشبه أن يكون هذا قول أبي يوسف؛ لما عرف من أ أنه . يصير وقفا بمجرد قوله: وقفت داري. Key Terms
توكيل بالطلاق (tawkil bi al-talaq): Delegation of the power of divorce to the wife; considered an oath-like empowerment, not a revocable agency
كلما (kullama): Every time; in legal context, implies repetition ad infinitum
وكالة معلقة (wakalah mu'allaqah): Conditional agency, activated upon fulfillment of a condition (e.g., removal)

A principal says to his agent: 'I appointed you on condition that whenever I remove you, you are my agent.' To terminate the agency permanently, what must the principal do?
A) Simply remove the agent once

Key Takeaway

Conditions for Valid Settlement (Sulḥ) with a Minor
Explaining when receipt is required in settlement and when a father can settle for a minor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition requiring receipt in a settlement and explain when a father can validly settle for a minor, distinguishing between cases with and without evidence.

Core Idea
Receipt in settlement is only required when the substitute is a debt for a debt, otherwise not.

This passage clarifies a crucial distinction in Hanafi ṣulḥ: when must the substitute be received immediately? The answer depends on whether the settlement involves a debt-for-debt exchange, which is prohibited without receipt. The text then applies this principle to a common scenario: a father settling a claim against his minor child. The validity hinges on whether the plaintiff has evidence and whether the settlement benefits the minor, providing a nuanced rule that balances guardianship and protection of the minor's property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule on receipt
The passage opens with the rule: 'Receipt of the substitute in settlement is a condition if it is debt for debt, otherwise not.' Determine what qualifies as 'debt for debt' (e.g., dirhams for dinars). Understand that if the settlement is on a non-debt item, immediate receipt is not required.
The prohibition of trading credit for credit (kālī’ bi kālī’) underlies this rule.
2
Understand the rationale for the debt-for-debt rule
When settlement is for something other than what was owed, it becomes a transaction (e.g., sale or exchange). If it is debt-for-debt, it falls under the prohibition of ribā, requiring immediate receipt to avoid uncertainty and potential interest.
The commentator references the hadith forbidding 'kālī’ bi kālī’.
3
Analyze the case of a father settling for a minor defendant
Consider the scenario: a man claims a house from a minor, and the father settles using the minor's property. The passage distinguishes based on the plaintiff's evidence. If the plaintiff has valid evidence, the settlement must be at least equivalent to the value (or slightly less, within the range people overlook) because the minor benefits by avoiding loss. If the plaintiff has no evidence or unjust evidence, the settlement is invalid because the father would be giving away the minor's property without benefit.
The father must act in the minor's best interest (wilāyah naẓariyyah).
4
Consider the father as the plaintiff
If the father himself is the plaintiff claiming on behalf of the minor and has no evidence, he may settle for any amount, even less than the value. Since ownership was not proven, the settlement secures some property for the minor and is pure benefit. However, if he has just evidence, it must be at or near the value.
This asymmetry highlights the principle that the guardian cannot be generous with the minor's property when the minor actually owns it (by evidence).
5
Summarize the key conditions
The settlement contract itself is valid if it avoids ribā (receipt when debt-for-debt). For a guardian settling for a minor, the additional condition is benefit to the minor. Benefit is assessed by comparing the substitute to the value and the plaintiff's evidence.
The tarjīḥ (preferred view) is that the father's settlement is valid only when it is beneficial, as confirmed by later authorities.

Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage is a ruling about conditions for valid settlement (sulh) and specifically its application when a father settles on behalf of a minor defendant. The main rule: in a settlement, receipt (qabd) of the substitute is a condition only if the settlement involves a debt for debt (e.g., dirhams for dinars, both in the obligation); otherwise, receipt is not required. The commentator explains that if the settlement is upon something other than what the creditor is owed, it becomes a transaction like a sale or exchange, and parting without receipt would involve ribā. The second part discusses when a father settles for a minor defendant. If the plaintiff has valid evidence (bayyinah), the father may settle for equivalent value or slightly more (within the amount people overlook), as the minor benefits by avoiding losing the asset. If the plaintiff has no evidence or unreliable evidence, the settlement is invalid because the father would be giving away the minor's property without benefit. However, if the father himself is the plaintiff (claiming on behalf of the minor) and has no evidence, he may settle for any amount, even much less than the value, because the minor had no proven ownership and the settlement secures some property. The passage also includes a brief note about accepting evidence after stating one has none, which is accepted due to possible forgetfulness.

Key Terms
صلح (ṣulḥ): A contract settling a dispute, exchanging a claim for an agreed substitute.
كالىء بكالىء (kālī’ bi kālī’): Trading credit for credit, which is prohibited due to ribā.
بينة (bayyinah): Valid legal evidence, usually testimony of two just witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) In all settlements.
B) Only when the settlement involves a debt for a debt (e.g., dirhams for dinars).
C) Only when one party is a minor.
D) Receipt is never required in settlement.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, receipt in ṣulḥ is required only for debt-for-debt exchanges; when a guardian settles for a minor, the settlement must benefit the minor, with the presence or absence of evidence determining the acceptable range of the substitute.

Condition of Taking Possession in Sulh (Debt-for-Debt)
Ruling on requirement of qabd in debt-for-debt sulh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when possession (qabd) is required in a sulh (compromise) and explain the ruling for compromises involving a minor based on the presence of evidence.

Core Idea
Possession is required in a debt-for-debt compromise, but not when the substitute is a specific asset.

This lesson examines a key condition in the Hanafi fiqh of sulh (compromise). The ruling distinguishes between compromises where the substitute is a debt in the dhimmah (debt-for-debt) and those where the substitute is a specific asset. In debt-for-debt situations, taking possession in the same session is a condition of validity, due to the prohibition of trading debt for debt. The passage also applies this principle to cases involving a minor, where the father or guardian acts on his behalf, and the presence or absence of evidence determines the validity and fairness of the compromise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of sulh
Read the opening line: 'قبض بدل الصلح شرط إن كان دينا بدين، وإلا لا.' Recognize that the ruling splits into two categories: when the substitute is a debt for a debt, and when it is not. Determine which category applies to the given case.
This distinction is fundamental: 'daynan bi dayn' triggers the possession requirement.
2
Apply the possession requirement
If the sulh is debt-for-debt, understand that possession (qabd) must occur in the same session. Without it, the transaction is invalid (fasid). If the substitute is a specific asset (muta'ayyin), no possession is required and separation is allowed immediately.
The hadith 'al-Kali' bi al-Kali' (spot for credit) prohibits deferred exchange of debts.
3
Analyze the minor scenario with evidence
The passage presents a case: a man claims a house from a minor, and the father makes a compromise using the minor's property. Follow the branches based on whether the claimant has just evidence (bayyinah 'adilah), no evidence, or unjust evidence. For each, determine the permissibility and the required value of the substitute.
The father's role changes: with evidence, he acts as a purchaser; without, he is a pure benefactor.
4
Distinguish father as guardian vs. father as claimant
If the father himself is the claimant for the minor (i.e., the minor is the plaintiff), the compromise is always valid, even if the substitute is less than the value. This is because no ownership was established for the minor in the first place, so the compromise brings pure benefit.
The executor (wasi) has the same authority as the father.

Taking possession of the substitute in a compromise is a condition if it is a debt for a debt, otherwise not. A man claimed a house from a minor, so the minor's father made a compromise using the minor's property. If the claimant has evidence, it is permissible if the substitute is equivalent to the value or more, within the range of what people overlook in transactions. If he has no evidence or it is not just, it is not permissible. He said: I have no evidence, then he brought proof, or said: I have no testimony, then he testified, it is accepted. Even if after the opponent's witness swore, it is not permissible. Do you not see that mere saying of the client: I revoked the agency, does not remove the agent; whenever he revokes, the agent remains until he revokes the conditional agency as detailed elsewhere. So I established the complete phrase in the text and made it match the text taken by the commentators. Memorize. Condition: if it occurs on dirhams for dinars, or on something else in the dhimmah; because when the compromise occurs on something other than what the creditor deserves by the loan contract, it is treated as a commutative contract, so it becomes a currency exchange or a sale, and in that, separation before taking possession is not allowed due to the prohibition of al-Kali' bi al-Kali'. Otherwise, if it is not a debt for a debt, taking possession is not required; because the compromise, when it occurs on a specific thing, it does not remain a debt in the dhimmah, so separation is permissible even if it involves riba, as when the compromise is on specific barley for wheat in the dhimmah, and it has passed before. 'Permissible' etc.: The compromise is permissible if its substitute is equivalent to the value or more than the value within the range of what people overlook; because there is benefit for the minor, which is the safety of the property; because if he does not compromise, the claimant takes it by evidence, so this compromise by the father is like a purchase from the claimant; and it is only permissible within what people overlook because he cannot avoid it. 'If he has no evidence' etc.: Means if the claimant has no evidence or it is not just, the compromise is invalid; because the father becomes a donor of the minor's property by the compromise, not a purchaser; because the claimant had no right to his property without the compromise, so there is no benefit for the minor in this compromise, rather there is harm, so it is not permissible because guardianship is based on consideration. If the father is the claimant for the minor and has no evidence, it is permissible in any case, even if the substitute is less than the value by a lot; because no ownership is established for the minor in what the father claimed, and no possibility of taking, so he is acquiring wealth for him by taking something out of the minor's possession in exchange, so it is pure benefit. If he has just evidence, it is not permissible except for the equivalent or less than the equivalent within the range of what people overlook; because he has become in the position of ownership due to his ability to take by evidence. The executor (wasi) in this is like the father because he stands in his place.
Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the fiqh of sulh (compromise). It addresses the requirement of qabd (taking possession) of the substitute in a sulh agreement. The ruling distinguishes between two scenarios: when the sulh involves a debt for a debt (dina bi-dayn), and when it does not. If the sulh is for a debt in exchange for another debt, taking possession is a condition (shart) for the validity of the transaction; if it is not a debt for debt, no possession is required. The commentator explains that when sulh involves a debt on both sides, it is treated as a sale or currency exchange, and the prohibition of trading debt for debt applies, hence possession must occur in the same session. The passage then applies this to a case where a man claims a house from a minor, and the father makes a compromise on the minor's behalf. The validity depends on whether the claimant has evidence. If he has just evidence, the compromise is valid only if the substitute is equivalent to the property's value or slightly more, because the father is effectively purchasing the property from the claimant for the minor's benefit. If he has no evidence or the evidence is not just, the compromise is invalid, as the father would be giving away the minor's property without benefit. However, if the father himself is the claimant for the minor (i.e., the minor is the plaintiff), it is always valid because it brings benefit by acquiring property. The executor (wasi) has the same authority as the father.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Taking physical or constructive possession of the substitute in a sulh.
صلح (sulh): A compromise or settlement between parties; here treated as a commutative contract when involving a substitute.
دينا بدين (daynan bi dayn): A transaction where both sides are debts.
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, typically two male witnesses or one male and two females.
وصي (wasi): Executor or guardian appointed to manage a minor's affairs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sulh where a person owes 100 dirhams and agrees to pay with a specific cow, is possession required in the same session?
A) Yes, because it is a sale.
B) No, because the cow is a specific asset (muta'ayyin).
C) Yes, because it is debt for a specific asset.
D) No, because the cow is not a debt.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a compromise (sulh) that involves a debt-for-debt exchange requires immediate possession to avoid the prohibited 'al-Kali' bi al-Kali', and when a guardian compromises for a minor, the presence of evidence determines whether he acts as a purchaser or a donor, affecting the fairness of the substitute.

Validity of Sale When Sultan Confiscates Property Without Specifying Sale
Ruling on sale under confiscation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between coercion on the act of sale and coercion on payment, and apply the Hanafi rule that a sale is valid if the seller voluntarily chooses to sell even under financial pressure.

Core Idea
Coercion on payment does not invalidate a sale; only coercion on the sale itself does.

This passage clarifies a key fiqh distinction: the difference between being forced to pay and being forced to sell. When a ruler demands money (confiscation) without ordering a specific sale, any sale you make to raise the money is voluntary—you chose to sell. The ruling is valid, just like a debtor selling his property to pay a debt. However, if the ruler orders you to sell your property, then a coerced sale is invalid unless you later willingly accept the price.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
First scenario: Sultan confiscates wealth (demands money) but does not specify how you must raise it. Second scenario: Sultan specifically orders you to sell your property or your sale is coerced.
The key is what action is coerced: payment or sale.
2
Analyze the locus of coercion
Determine whether the coercion (ikrah) directly targets the act of selling or merely the obligation to pay. In the first scenario, the coercion is on payment—you are forced to pay, but you choose to sell. In the second, the coercion is on the sale itself.
Hanafi usul: coercion negates consent only if it directly targets the act.
3
Apply the analogy with the imprisoned debtor
The author compares to a creditor who imprisons a debtor for debt. If the debtor sells his property to pay, the sale is valid because the coercion is on the payment, not the sale. The same logic applies to the Sultan's demand.
The asl (original case) is the debtor; the far' (new case) is the confiscated person. The illa (effective cause) is that coercion is on payment only.
4
Understand the exception when sale is coerced
If the Sultan specifies 'sell this property' or orders you to sell, and you sell under duress, the sale is invalid unless you later willingly accept the price (i.e., retrospective ratification).
This is because the sale itself becomes coerced.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صادره السلطان ولم يعين بيع ماله فباع ماله صح. بل طلب منه جملة المال. صح أي بيعه؛ لأنه غير مكره به وإنما باع باختياره غاية الأمر أنه احتاج إلى بيعه لإيفاء ما طلب منه، وذلك لا يوجب الكره، كالدائن إذا حبس المديون بالدين فباع ماله ليقضي بثمنه دينه، فإنه يجوز؛ لأنه باعه باختياره، وإنما وقع الكره في الإيفاء لا في البيع. وإنما قيد بقوله: 'لم يعين بيع ماله'؛ لأنه لو عين بيع ماله، أو أمره بالبيع فباعه مكرها، لا يصح إلا أن يأخذ الثمن طوعا.
The Sultan confiscated his property and did not specify the sale of his property, so he sold his property, it is valid. Rather, he demanded the total wealth from him. 'Valid' means his sale is valid; because he is not forced thereby; rather, he sold by his choice, the only issue is that he needed to sell to fulfill what was demanded, and that does not cause coercion, like a creditor who imprisons a debtor for debt and then he sells his property to pay the debt with its price; it is valid because he sold by his choice; coercion only occurred in payment, not in the sale. He (author) restricted it by saying 'did not specify the sale of his property' because if he specified the sale of his property, or ordered him to sell and he sold under coercion, it is not valid unless he takes the price willingly.
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where the Sultan (ruler) confiscates a person's wealth without specifically ordering the sale of his property. In such a case, if the person sells his property voluntarily to meet the demand, the sale is valid. The reasoning is that the coercion is directed at the payment of the debt, not at the sale itself. The person sells by his own choice, even if he is under pressure to pay. This is analogous to a debtor who is imprisoned for debt and then sells his property to pay; the sale is valid. However, if the Sultan explicitly specifies that the property must be sold or orders the person to sell, and the person sells under coercion, the sale is not valid unless he accepts the price willingly afterward.

Key Terms
مصادرة (musadarah): Confiscation of property by the ruler
إكراه (ikrah): Coercion that nullifies free consent

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the Sultan demands money without specifying a sale, what determines the validity of a person's sale to raise funds?
A) Whether the Sultan approves the price
B) Whether the sale is voluntary (no direct coercion on the sale)
C) Whether the person sells to a specific buyer
D) Whether the person sells at market price

Key Takeaway
A sale made under financial duress is valid in the Hanafi school as long as the coercion is on the obligation to pay, not on the act of selling itself.
